Huang Musong Arrives in the Capital and Plans to Pay Respects to Lin and Wang Immediately 8

Report on the Journey to Tibet Has Been Drafted

[Nanjing] Huang Musong arrived in the capital from Shanghai at 2:30 PM on the 16th. Representatives from various agencies were sent to the station to welcome him. Wang [Jingwei] sent Chen Rui as his representative to convey his regards. After disembarking, Huang went to his residence to rest, received friends from the capital, and asked Lin and Wang for an audience to report on his journey to Tibet. Wang scheduled to host a reception for Huang at the Executive Yuan on the afternoon of the 17th. Huang said that he has drafted a report on his journey to Tibet and will submit it to the central government after it has been completed. While in the capital, he will pay his respects to Chairman Chiang in Jiangxi after his affairs have been settled and report on the journey. (Special dispatch, 16th)

[Nanjing] Huang Musong spoke about his journey to Tibet, saying, "I departed last April and arrived in Chengdu, then proceeded west by land. I arrived in Lhasa in mid-August. I stayed in Tibet for three months and traveled to Nepal and India at the end of November. On January 3rd, I traveled by sea eastwards and also conveniently visited various islands in Southeast Asia. In total, the journey lasted ten months and covered 20,000 li. Although it was arduous, it is what one should do for the country. The general situation in Tibet is good, and there is a strong sense of orientation. There is also no problem with the Panchen Lama returning to Tibet. After completing the memorial service, I received a telegram from Prime Minister Yudha of Nepal, inviting me to visit. I stayed there for four or five days and was impressed by the country's good political construction and other conditions. On the way back east, I visited Penang Island and Batavia, where Chinese compatriots held meetings to welcome me and showed great concern for the motherland. In particular, the Dutch in the Dutch East Indies have greatly changed their attitude towards Chinese compatriots due to China's recent efforts to build a unified nation. My stay in the Philippines was relatively short. I passed through Hong Kong and Guangzhou and transferred to a ship northwards. I did not meet with President Wang in Shanghai. I will report to the central government and Wang in the next few days and then go to Jiangxi to meet with Chairman Chiang in a few days, but the date of departure has not yet been determined." (Central News Agency dispatch, 16th)

Chiang Discusses the Necessity of Sino-Japanese Cooperation with Japanese Journalists 9

The Principle of Morality as the Fundamental Principle for Resolving Sino-Japanese Difficulties

The Northeast Problem as an Important Factor in National Antipathy

Economic Cooperation Should Be Based on Sincerity of Mutual Assistance and Mutual Benefit

Kuling: Chairman Chiang's interview with reporters from the Tokyo and Osaka Asahi Shimbun on the 14th included the following remarks:

Japanese Reporter: (1) In terms of the overall situation in East Asia, Sino-Japanese cooperation is necessary. What are the methods of cooperation? Chairman Chiang: (Answer) Sino-Japanese cooperation is not only necessary from the perspective of the overall situation in East Asia but also for the sake of the world's overall situation, because East Asia has only two countries, China and Japan, and these two countries are also important members of the world. As for Sino-Japanese cooperation, it should first start from the principle of morality, and then it will not be difficult to concretely realize cooperation.

(2) What are your opinions of Japan and the Japanese people? Please give us your frank advice. (Answer) Since the Meiji Restoration, I have admired your country's rapid progress and the general public's virtues of loyalty, filial piety, friendship, etiquette, diligence, and thrift. However, it would be regrettable if you abandon the inherent spirit of Eastern culture and are dominated by the ideology of valuing power and rejecting reason.

(3) Is there a fundamental solution to the current difficulties between China and Japan? (Answer) I have always believed that the principle of morality is the fundamental principle for resolving the current difficulties between China and Japan. Since you are a news reporter who hopes for Sino-Japanese cooperation, you should first thoroughly understand the true psychology of the Chinese people. Not only is there no anti-Japanese action or ideology in China, but there is also no reason to be anti-Japanese. However, the Chinese people generally have a deep-seated anti-Qing sentiment, that is, an ideology that rejects the rule of the Qing dynasty. After 300 years of continuous struggle, they were finally freed from the shackles of the Manchurian evil government. The entire Chinese people still have extremely painful memories. Since the Northeast Problem has evolved to the current stage, the trauma has deepened. This ideology can be said to be deeply rooted and extremely difficult to eliminate. If the Northeast Problem remains as it is today, this antipathy will deepen daily. The accumulation of historical facts cannot be eliminated by any force. Therefore, in studying whether Sino-Japanese cooperation can be realized, one must not ignore the important factor of this national psychology.

(4) What are the Chairman's views on changing anti-Japanese attitudes, improving relations between the two countries, especially in education? (Answer) China has always advocated good faith, peace, and hoped to enhance cooperation with friendly countries. Hostile concepts have never been adopted. The same is true in education, which always focuses on cultivating the virtues of benevolence, love, and mutual assistance. For the sake of healthy national thought, attention should be paid to correcting anything that violates this spirit and is sufficient to cause hostile feelings. However, regarding education and thought, both countries must pay the same attention and make the same efforts. The avoidance of aggression and humiliation against China will no longer cause any stimulation or resentment to our people, and it is possible to fundamentally improve our relations.

(5) What are your thoughts on Sino-Japanese economic cooperation? (Answer) There is a prerequisite for this matter. We should first improve the current situation between the two countries and restore normal relations. Then, rational and mutually beneficial pure economic cooperation will not only be possible but also necessary. However, there should be sincerity of mutual assistance and mutual benefit between each other and not contain other effects.

(6) What are the Chairman's thoughts on Foreign Minister Hirota's speech on China policy? (Answer) Although Foreign Minister Hirota's speech on China policy was very abstract, we have deep feelings about it. At least it can be said to be the starting point for the improvement of Sino-Japanese relations. I think Foreign Minister Hirota will be able to prove the content of his speech with future facts. At the same time, our people can also gain a new understanding of Japan as a result.

(7) It seems that the steps taken by the Kuomintang for national rejuvenation are somewhat too hasty, which naturally gives rise to a tendency to exclude foreigners, especially between China and Japan, which easily causes disputes. What is your opinion on this? (Answer) The purpose of the National Revolution led by Sun Yat-sen is only to seek freedom and equality for China. China has recently been striving to build a modern country in the spirit of independence and self-reliance, which should not cause foreign disputes.

(8) In the past, I believe that diplomatic methods are easier to solve problems between China and Japan. I think the most appropriate way to solve the issue in the future is with sincerity. What is your opinion on this? (Answer) I believe that Sino-Japanese problems can only be solved by relying on justice, and they can only be solved through diplomatic methods.

(9) Regarding the Pan-Asianism advocated by Japan, please criticize it frankly from China's position. (Answer) Regarding Pan-Asianism, please refer to Sun Yat-sen's writings, and you will understand my meaning.

(10) Personally, I believe that China needs a considerable degree of dictatorship. What does the Chairman think? (Answer) China's national conditions are different from those of Italy and Germany and are not suitable for dictatorship.

(11) May I ask who is the most admired figure in Chinese history by the Chairman? (Answer) There are many admirable sages and philosophers in Chinese history. The one I have personally followed and admired all my life is Sun Yat-sen.

(12) Does the Chairman respect any Japanese figures, ancient or modern? Who are they? (Answer) Rai Sanyo before the Meiji Restoration, and Katsu Kaishu and Yoshida Shoin among the Meiji luminaries are all figures I admire. (Central News Agency dispatch, 16th)

Jiangsu Provincial Government Pays Attention to Developing the Fishing Industry 11

[Nanjing] To develop the fishing industry, the Jiangsu Provincial Government has transferred a loan of one million yuan from the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Fund to purchase fishing vessels. This loan has been approved, and the provincial government is drafting a detailed plan, a purchase list, and a repayment plan for review. Once the contract is signed, the fishing grounds of Jiangsu Province extend from Haizhou in the north to Songjiang in the south, and from the coast of Jiangsu Province in the west to Japan and Korea in the east. The total area of marine fishing grounds reaches over 103,500 square miles, of which the inshore fishing area is about 30,000 square miles. There are many islands in the sea, and the seabed along the coast is flat. There are thousands of kinds of marine life. If fishing is properly managed, there is indeed great benefit. (Special dispatch, 16th)

Japan Plans to First Return Political Power

Withdrawal of Troops Still Pending

Great Fire in Xingcheng County Seat 15

Japanese Army Seizes Civilian Guns

[Tianjin] The fire in Wudao Street, Xingcheng County, on the 11th did not extinguish until the evening of the 12th. The entire street was burned to ashes. The Japanese army tightly closed the four gates and searched for resistance elements. Many innocent people were shot and killed. The cause of the fire was that the Japanese army forced residents to hand over their self-defense guns and promised to pay a price, but after they were handed over, they did not give a penny. The Japanese army searched the densely populated Wudao Street. In the house of Yu Zhizhong, they found one gun and ten bullets and said that Yu had violated the law by plotting rebellion and immediately shot him and his son. This sparked a civil uprising. More than a hundred strong men resisted with private guns and were surrounded and dispersed by a large Japanese army. More than half of them were killed. (Special dispatch, 16th)

Executive Yuan Plans to Formulate Measures to Relieve the Drought in Hunan Province 20

When I have a little time, I plan to go to Lushan to pay my respects to Chairman Chiang. The date of departure has not been determined. The original plan to return to Fujian is now a thing of the past." (Special dispatch, 16th)

Current Commentary

U.S. Military Buildup 22

— Respectfully

When Japan declared the abolishment of the naval ratios stipulated in the Washington and London treaties at the end of last year, both Britain and the United States remained calm. Firstly, the treaties still had two years of effect. Secondly, Japan's financial resources were limited. Britain and the United States understood that Japan would not dare to rashly initiate a naval arms race. It has been more than a month since the beginning of this year. There has been no sign of any deterioration in the naval issue among the three countries. Even Japan, which first advocated the removal of naval ratios with the intention of dominating the Western Pacific, is promoting the return to normalcy in its diplomacy with Britain and the United States. For example, Japan's public opinion has remained calm regarding the recent exclusion of Japanese immigrant farmers in Arizona, USA, which shows its general attitude.

However, in terms of naval strength, it is expected that when the naval treaties expire next year, the Japanese navy will have 754,000 tons, with no obsolete ships. The United States claims to have 1.2 million tons, but many cruisers, aircraft carriers, destroyers, and submarines have not yet been completed, and its actual strength is probably no more than 940,000 tons. Britain claims to have 1.22 million tons, but has 94,000 tons of unfinished ships and 60,000 tons of old ships, with an actual strength of only 1.066 million tons. Destroyers and submarines are useful tools for coastal warfare, and Japan has an absolute advantage in these two categories. Even the ratio of light and heavy cruisers, compared with Britain and the United States, exceeds 71 percent. In terms of attack, it may be insufficient, but in terms of self-defense, it is more than adequate.

U.S. President Roosevelt, aware of the urgency of the international crisis, has expressed sympathy for the arguments of the military expansion faction and intends to actively implement a $2 billion national defense plan. If this plan can be implemented, the United States' territory along the Pacific Ocean can be as solid as a rock and will no longer be in danger of being invaded. In addition, former Air Force Commander Major General Mitchell has been advocating an airship policy, proposing to use 50 Zeppelin-style airships to reach any country in Asia when necessary and bomb it. Recently, the Army Committee also plans to invest 11 million gold dollars in building a large air force base in Hawaii, 2 million gold dollars in building fortresses along the Pacific coast for defense, 8 million gold dollars in strengthening the garrison troops in various fortresses, and 90 million gold dollars in increasing military armored aircraft by 800, bringing the number of modern new aircraft in its army to more than 2,300.

The reasons for the United States' military expansion plan are: First, it recognizes the Hawaiian Islands as part of its own territory, which is completely different from the Philippine Islands. Second, modern transportation is becoming increasingly developed. The flight distance between San Francisco and Honolulu is only 15 hours. Therefore, for the sake of self-defense, it is especially necessary to actively rectify the air force. Third, the Washington Treaty imposed restrictions on the defense projects of the Philippines, Guam, and the Aleutian Islands. Therefore, Hawaii must be its foremost line of defense.

Japan, which is implicitly in a hostile position with the United States, is probably particularly wary of the American expansion of its air force. Therefore, in addition to the so-called second air force supplementary plan, it is also preparing a third supplement to completely update the aircraft belonging to both the army and navy, replacing the old ones with new aircraft with long-distance endurance, striving to be able to stop the American aircraft's offensive. We all know that the Japanese are most concerned about the bombing of their country by enemy air forces. Its borders are surrounded by the sea, which is a natural barrier. Before the development of three-dimensional warfare, it could indeed boast of its safety. Who knew that with the development of the air force, which changes with each passing day, its geographical advantages have already lost their basis, and the wooden buildings in its major cities still account for more than 80 percent of the total. Once it is attacked by the air force, even if it puts all its efforts into defense, it will still be enough to affect the overall situation. Therefore, the United States' enthusiasm for the expansion of its air force is probably for this reason. In short, although there has been no special development in the naval issue recently, the confrontational situation between Britain, the United States, and Japan is still very tense.

Hauptmann, Convicted in Lindbergh Kidnapping Case, Pleads Innocence 23

Hiring a Lawyer to Draft a Document to Raise Funds for Appeal

Claims He Can Swear to God That He Cannot Plead Guilty

Flemington - Hauptmann, who was sentenced to death in the Lindbergh kidnapping and murder case, today asked his lawyer, Reilly, to issue a statement stating that the trial was improper. He said, "I swear to God that I was not involved in the kidnapping and murder case. Apart from what I have confessed to the court, I have absolutely no knowledge of this case or the ransom. What I am now asking for is justice and public assistance in order to obtain this justice. God is my judge. I cannot plead guilty because there is no guilt to plead. If someone comes to me and says, 'If you make a declaration, you can be released,' then I will answer, 'I have already confessed everything I know to the court.'" This document requests public donations for appeal expenses. A reporter visited Hauptmann, who said that the most absurd thing in the trial was the wood board in my attic. You must know that there is a lot of lumber in my garage. Why would I go to the attic to get a wood board? He also said that Lindbergh's presence in the courtroom during the trial certainly had an impact on the jurors. The New York police chief stated today that, as far as New York is concerned, the Lindbergh kidnapping case has not ended. This is a case in New Jersey, but if someone wants to arrest criminals in New York, it is certainly our business. At the same time, the New York Daily News stated that there are more than just three people involved in the ransom fraud case, but the New York police have already found the second person and are planning to arrest him. When Lindbergh was sitting in the car, waiting for Dr. Condon to return from the cemetery (the location where the ransom was paid), this person, with his head wrapped in a towel, peeked into Lindbergh's car. New Jersey did not mention this second person when trying this case because it wanted to end the case quickly and did not want to involve too many people. In fact, the police in the Department of Justice in New York and New Jersey have long known that Hauptmann had an accomplice. (Reuters, 15th)

Flemington - After Hauptmann was sentenced to death, his lawyer solicited donations from the public on his behalf in order to use the funds raised for appeal expenses. A total of 70 dollars were raised on the first day. Hauptmann recently received a telegram from his mother in Germany, saying, "I firmly believe that you are innocent and that the truth will eventually come to light." Hauptmann's mother also sent a telegram to New Jersey Governor Hoffman, saying, "During the European War, two sons and my husband all died on the battlefield. I am seventy years old this year, and I cannot bear another blow. Please, Governor, grant my son amnesty to avoid his death." The Governor recently said that Hauptmann's case should first be decided by the appellate court, and finally it can be reviewed by the "Court of Pardons." (Note: The Governor is one of the judges of the Court of Pardons.) (Havas, 15th)

Principles of Bankruptcy Law Determined 33

Public Release of Germany's Reply to the Anglo-French Declaration of London: Shared Desire for Peace, Willing to Negotiate Individually with All Nations 65

Acceptance Expressed Only for the Conclusion of an Air Convention

No Mention of the League of Nations or Central and Eastern European Pacts

[Berlin] Germany's reply to the London Protocol has been simultaneously published in Berlin, London, and Paris. The document begins by stating that the German government shares the sincere desire of the British and French governments to promote peace, as the preservation of peace is not only beneficial to other countries but also to Germany. Therefore, Germany greatly welcomes the open discussion of the Anglo-French proposals. The German government is willing to submit the complex European issues raised in the first part of the Anglo-French proposal for detailed review, taking into consideration Germany's geographical environment to ensure its security. The German government is particularly willing to consider how to avoid the dangers of an arms race, as this problem is entirely the result of various countries failing to adhere to the disarmament clauses of various peace treaties. Germany firmly believes that only through free discussion can the issue of armaments be thoroughly resolved. The document also welcomes the conclusion of an anti-aircraft convention, and Germany is willing to use its air force as a sanction against those who disrupt peace. However, before formally participating in negotiations, it wishes to conduct preliminary consultations with various governments individually. Finally, the document states that Germany fully agrees with the British and French governments that the conclusion of an anti-aircraft convention is indeed a way to stabilize Europe. (National Telegram, 15th)

[London] Germany's reply to the suggestions proposed by England and France on February 3rd, as expected, has been published in Berlin tonight. It expresses welcome to the conclusion of a five-nation air convention by England, France, Germany, Belgium, and Italy. The reply states that the German government is prepared, in principle, to use its air force to suppress disturbances to peace; therefore, it sincerely hopes to promptly obtain the free consent of the governments concerned, seeking methods to ensure that this convention guarantees the maximum possible security for the signatory states. However, discussions on many aspects are not yet fully prepared, which can easily lead to conflicts. To conclude an air convention, such negotiations should be avoided. The German government believes that before participating in such negotiations, it should, through separate agreements with the governments concerned, clarify several fundamental issues of principle. Therefore, the German government sincerely hopes that the British government will first exchange views directly with the German government, as the British government is a party to the London talks and a guarantor of the Locarno Treaty. The British government believes that the conclusion of an air convention will be an important step towards the unity of European nations, leading to a satisfactory resolution of other European issues. The German government expresses great sympathy for this view. The German government, like the British and French governments, also holds the utmost sincerity in promoting and preserving peace; therefore, it sincerely welcomes the spirit of friendship and trust expressed by England and France in encouraging discussions among governments. The reply continues by stating that the German government is willing to thoroughly study the European issues raised in the first part of the London communiqué with the same spirit of attention to peace and German security. The German government is particularly attentive to studying the dangers of an arms race and how to avoid them in the future, as such dangers have already arisen since heavily armed nations failed to fulfill the disarmament provisions stipulated in treaties. Only the spirit of free compromise among sovereign states, as expressed in the London communiqué, can lead to a permanent international resolution of the scope of armaments. The reply makes no mention of the Anglo-French suggestion that Germany rejoin the League of Nations, nor does it mention the Central and Eastern European Pact, which is particularly noteworthy. The German government has separately sent this reply to the French and Italian governments. Because British cabinet members do not have time to discuss it, there has been no comment from official circles in London. According to opinions in diplomatic circles, the reply only expresses acceptance of the air convention. The British and French governments will naturally need a long period of consideration before they can decide whether the reply is satisfactory. (Reuters, 15th)

Britain and France Consider Procedures for Negotiations with Germany 66

Diplomacy Enters a Phase of Activity

[London] The matter of Britain sending a cabinet member to Berlin has not yet been considered. The Foreign Office is currently studying the content of Germany's reply in detail. The impression of disappointment here last night has been confirmed by diplomatic figures. Britain and France will soon exchange views in order to decide on procedures for conducting negotiations with Germany. (Havas, 16th)

[Paris] Opinion here is the same as in London, believing that after consulting with each other, France and England should send another official document to Berlin. This morning, British newspapers suggested that Britain could hold a separate conversation with Germany once. Even if the British government accepts this proposal, and Germany expresses agreement, France and England should still send a new official document to Berlin. Negotiations between the two countries regarding Germany's reply will probably proceed through diplomatic channels on Monday. The French government is scheduled to hold a cabinet meeting on Tuesday, and the British cabinet meeting will also be held on Wednesday, in order to determine the position of the two governments. From then on, negotiations between the two countries will enter a phase of activity. (Havas, 16th)

Impression from London 67

A New Phase of Diplomatic Negotiations Begins

Situation Shows Some Improvement

[London] Today's newspapers offer many criticisms of Germany's reply to England and France, all stating that the reply is vague and lacks concrete proposals. What is welcome is Germany's declaration of support for peace and opposition to armaments. The Times states that the Anglo-French suggestions have been accepted by Germany, considering it the starting point of a new phase of diplomatic negotiations. Therefore, this reply, in its nature as a preliminary response, is an indication of preparation for negotiations. The Daily Telegraph reports that Germany has not catered to the will of England and France, but at least it is not resentful. The reply has brought some progress to the situation, but not as good as expected when the Anglo-French plan was first announced. (Reuters, 16th)

[London] Today's newspapers offer many criticisms of Germany's reply to England and France, all stating that the reply is vague and lacks concrete proposals. What is welcome is Germany's declaration of support for peace and opposition to armaments. The Times states that the Anglo-French suggestions have been accepted by Germany, considering it the starting point of a new phase of diplomatic negotiations. Therefore, this reply, in its nature as a preliminary response, is an indication of preparation for negotiations. The Daily Telegraph reports that Germany has not catered to the will of England and France, but at least it is not resentful. The reply has brought some progress to the situation, but not as good as expected when the Anglo-French plan was first announced. (Reuters, 16th)

[London] The impression caused by the German reply to the Anglo-French London Declaration is clearly unfavorable. It is generally believed that Britain and France need to hold consultations immediately, as the British cabinet believes that the consistency of opinion between Britain and France determined in the London Declaration of February 3 should be maintained. The subsequent reply to Germany should be decided only after Britain and France have consulted and agreed with each other, or whether this reply is indeed necessary, as the German reply does not indicate non-acceptance but is deliberately ambiguous. What intentions does Germany have regarding the Treaty guaranteeing the independence of Austria, the Eastern European Mutual Assistance Pact, and the issue of Germany rejoining the League of Nations? The general public hopes for a clear understanding, and it is generally believed that the proposals put forward in the London Declaration of February 3 are interconnected and inseparable, including the air convention. If other parts of the London Declaration are not accepted, then the air convention cannot be concluded. However, British opinion is that although the various proposals are interconnected, it is still possible to exchange views separately on the air convention and other points. Regarding the Eastern European Pact, it is believed that if the signatory countries are substantially prepared to provide mutual assistance, then the drafting and implementation of the pact can be mutually discussed and slightly accommodated by the countries concerned, with the original purpose of the Eastern European Pact as a necessary condition. Furthermore, in the German reply, criticism is leveled at the victorious nations for not fulfilling the disarmament provisions stipulated in the Treaty of Versailles. People here have severely criticized this, as the British and French declarations have repeatedly and cautiously avoided mentioning Germany's secret expansion of armaments in violation of the Treaty of Versailles. Germany's retort can be described as extremely unwise. How to respond to the German reply will probably be negotiated immediately by Britain and France through diplomatic channels. If the outcome of the negotiations deems it beneficial for Britain to send a cabinet member to Germany, then the Lord Privy Seal, Eden, may be ordered to go to Berlin, but at present, everything cannot be speculated. (Havas, 15th)

Eden's Declaration 68

[London] The Lord Privy Seal, Eden, recently issued a declaration stating that the Anglo-French London talks have yielded results and will have infinite benefits. He also stated that the resolution of the Saar issue and the South Hungarian dispute by the League of Nations Council of Administration last December was of great importance, and that the establishment of the Rome Agreement by France and Italy afterwards has opened a new era for European reconstruction and the restoration of trust. The conclusion is that the League of Nations Council is now in a much stronger position than it was six months ago, and the collective peace system is consistently superior to the balance of power system, which has never been able to absolutely guarantee peace. (Havas, 15th)

Chancellor of the Exchequer's Statement 69

[London] The Chancellor of the Exchequer, Chamberlain, delivered a speech to voters, mentioning the issue of a Western European air convention. He stated that if Britain is to assume certain new obligations, it should have the ability to fulfill them. An air force alone is insufficient and must be supplemented by considerable naval and land forces for the air force to be effective. (Havas, 10th)

Paris Maintains a Calm Attitude 70

Recognizes that the Future of Negotiations is Difficult

But the Door to Understanding Remains Open

[Paris] It is expected here that the British and French governments, after consultation, will soon jointly reply to the German telegram. A certain important French figure told a Reuters interviewer here today, "Our attitude is extremely calm. It would be especially welcome if the German dispatch referred to the Eastern European or Central European pacts, and not just the air convention. But Germany may believe that the Eastern European Pact and the Rome Agreement are currently in progress, so there is no need for the dispatch to involve them." (Reuters, 16th)

[Paris] Responsible figures here are not very surprised by the German memorandum answering the Anglo-French London suggestions. They believe that although the German reply cannot be said to have expressed agreement, it has at least not closed the door to future understanding. To seek future understanding, it is necessary to go through lengthy negotiations, and these negotiations will be extremely difficult. Now it is just the beginning. Germany has not paid attention to the various issues raised in the London Declaration, but has uniquely emphasized the conclusion of an air convention, believing that the air convention means allowing Germany to establish an air force, which is quite noteworthy. In the German reply, no mention is made of the Kinau River Convention (i.e., the Central European Pact guaranteeing Austria's independence) and the Eastern European Mutual Assistance Pact, probably because Germany requested France and Italy in early February to provide a detailed explanation of the Danube River Convention, and France also sent a note to the German government in January of this year, replying to the German memorandum of September 10 last year regarding the Eastern European Mutual Assistance Pact. Germany needs to reply to this French note separately, so neither matter was mentioned in this reply to England and France. In addition, the fact that the German reply did not mention the League of Nations is also noteworthy to responsible figures here. It is probably that the German government believes that Germany's position on the League of Nations over the past two years has been very clear and does not need to be explained further. If so, whether the issue of Germany rejoining the League of Nations can be finally decided only after other issues have been resolved is a question. In short, all issues should be negotiated simultaneously and cannot be separated. This is the basic principle of the London Declaration. It is incomprehensible why the German reply does not express an opinion on this basic principle. However, the British and French governments should firmly maintain the principles and text of the London Declaration from beginning to end. Also, according to the London Declaration, a general arms limitation convention must be signed first, and the Eastern European and Danube River conventions should be signed at the same time to replace the arms clauses in Part V of the Treaty of Versailles. The German reply avoids expressing an opinion on the possibility of concluding this general arms limitation convention. Even more noteworthy is that the German reply implicitly indicates the reasons on which Germany's policy of rearming is based: due to the fact that heavily armed countries have not complied with the provisions of the Treaty of Versailles to implement arms reduction, it should be known that the governments of England, France, the United States, Italy, and Germany clearly stipulated in the declaration made on December 11, 1932, the method of gradually reducing armaments, which has been recognized by important German government officials, and in October 1933, when Germany announced its withdrawal from the League of Nations, the three countries of England, France, and the United States also proposed a plan for gradually reducing armaments, which shows that Germany's accusations do not conform to the facts. In addition, the German note suggests that the leaders of the British and German governments hold informal talks. If this procedure can facilitate the resolution of various outstanding issues, then the French government should naturally be pleased. In short, the note submitted by the German government to the British and French ambassadors in Germany yesterday must be carefully studied in Paris and London together before negotiations can continue. (Havas, 15th)

[Paris] The memorandum from Germany regarding the Anglo-French declaration has been published in all morning newspapers today, becoming the material for discussions in political circles. The parliamentary discussion of this case last night was very heated. According to external speculation, the content of the reply will be nothing more than two points: (1) the wording will be very gentle, and (2) the door to all developments will be fully open. People here are very uneasy about Germany's intention to negotiate with Britain first, because this action is tantamount to demolishing the cooperation between Britain and France. The French embassy in Britain issued a message last night, stating that the British and French governments, in view of Germany's attitude, are willing to reconsider the London Declaration. This decision is supported by all newspapers that are concerned about world peace. A small magazine stated that Germany's reply has nothing other than the inherent color of German diplomacy in recent years. However, since the path is not blocked, we must maintain a patient attitude. If the Germans can recognize the indivisibility of the London Declaration, then the result will be satisfactory. The Petit Parisien believes that Germany's reply must be very cold. On the surface, Germany does not oppose the Anglo-French suggestions, but it has implicitly shelved these suggestions. Another newspaper finds it strange that the German reply does not mention the most important parts of the London suggestions. L'Industrie believes that the German reply is very cunning. Le Matin advocates against being dogmatic and opposes immediately accusing Germany of demanding equality but not being willing to pay the price, because it is now in the initial stage of talks. Although the situation may be smooth or rough in the future, as long as there is sincerity, the door to negotiations will never be closed. (National Telegram, 16th)

Rome Maintains Silence 71

Maintains Friendship with England and France

[Rome] The German government's reply to the Anglo-French London Declaration of February 3 has been reprinted in important positions in the newspapers here, but without any criticism, so as not to hinder the negotiations of the countries concerned. This is in line with the attitude that the government should take during the initial negotiations. Political figures suspected that Germany might be delaying things even before the German reply was published, and they are even more worried at this moment. However, it is generally believed that the friendship between Italy, France, and England has become a major fact and should be maintained. (Havas, 16th)

Views of Polish Figures 72

Warsaw Today's newspapers mostly do not comment on the reply sent by Germany to the British and French governments. Only the government newspaper "Polish Express" stated, "The London Agreement was a shaky building, and Germany's reply has torn down its walls." The Polish government's feelings about the recent London Agreement can be seen in this statement. (Havas, 15th)

British Royal Airship Crashes En Route from Naples to Malta 78

Thick Fog Causes Impact with Mountain Peak, Resulting in Instant Fire

Four Military Officers and Experts Killed

Messina – A British Royal Air Force airship, en route from Naples to the Kalafrana seaplane base in Malta this morning, crashed on a mountainside near Messina in Sicily. Three aviation officers and one aviation technical expert were killed. The airship, equipped with four engines, was one of four en route from Britain to Singapore. The only eyewitness to the crash was a farmer digging on the hillside. He stated that the entire mountain was shrouded in fog and the sky was filled with clouds. At approximately 9:30 AM, as he looked up at the sky, he suddenly saw an aircraft descending from the clouds, one wing up and one wing down. The lower wing of the aircraft appeared to have struck the mountainside, and a dense cloud of smoke immediately erupted, followed by a loud explosion. According to his account, the aircraft was already on fire before it hit the mountain. After impact, it shattered into pieces and fell onto the hillside. He immediately rushed to the scene and saw two people in front of the aircraft, their bodies half-burned. However, due to the intense flames, he could not approach. He then found a section of the aircraft body some distance away and rushed to San Filippo to report to the local authorities. The official immediately led Red Cross workers to the crash site to collect the charred remains. Shortly thereafter, heavy rain began to fall, and the work was suspended. Due to nightfall, it had to be postponed until the next morning. At that time, only three bodies had been recovered. The Royal Air Force has begun a thorough investigation into the cause of the crash. The Admiralty has dispatched a warship to transport the remains of the four victims back to England. (Reuters, 16th)

Famous French Aviators Attempt Non-Stop Flight to South America 79

Departed for Brazil at 6 AM Yesterday

Istres – Codos and Rossi, who set the world record for long-distance flight, took off from here at 6:36 AM this morning to attempt the first non-stop flight from France to South America. The two aviators are now heading for the capital of Brazil. If the weather is favorable, they may break their record of 6,690 miles set last August. Last year, the two flew from New York to Syria without landing. The aircraft they are using this time is equipped with a six-horsepower engine and has a speed of 150 miles per hour. (Reuters, 16th)

Discussions in Tianjin Regarding Issues in the War Zone 95

Doihara's Instructions

Yin Tao Expresses Extreme Optimism

Tianjin Dispatch: Yin Tong, Yin Rugeng, and Tao Shangming arrived in Tianjin on the evening of the 10th with Takahashi, a military attache from the Japanese Embassy, to discuss various unresolved issues in the war zone. Knowing that Iwaga would arrive in Tianjin from Yu on the 11th to meet Doihara, they arranged to come to Tianjin to discuss the matter together. At 2:00 PM on the 11th, the two Yins and Tao Shangming went to the Tokiwa Inn in the Japanese Concession to visit Doihara and meet Takahashi. Under Doihara's instructions, they briefly exchanged views on matters in the war zone. At 2:00 PM, Takahashi accompanied Yin Rugeng to visit Meijin, the commander of the Japanese garrison, at the Japanese military camp in Haiguang Temple. At 3:00 PM, Yin Rugeng left and went to the Provincial Government to visit Yu Xuezhong to discuss the principles of the negotiations on the eastward deployment of the newly formed special task force in the Gaoyi war zone. At 2:30 PM, Iwaga arrived in Tianjin from Yu via the Pingyu train and waited at the Tokiwa Inn. The two Yins and Tao Shangming visited again and had a long talk in Room 10 of the inn. The matters discussed at the time were: (1) the issue of the exchange of garrisons for the newly formed Hebei War Zone Special Police Force; (2) the issue of cracking down on Japanese and Korean thugs in Luanle and restricting the forcible opening of drug dens; (3) the issue of reorganizing the Yutian Security Supplementary Team and Wang Bingxiao's local militia; (4) the issue of taking over the Eastern Mausoleum of Malanyu. The discussion lasted for three hours and ended at 6:30 PM. After the meeting, Yin Tong hosted a banquet at the Beining official residence on Haihe Road to entertain the guests. Iwaga and Takahashi sent Doihara off on the train south on the 12th and then went to Ping. Yin Rugeng and Tao Shangming returned to Ping and Tang on the 12th and 13th to begin discussing the contents of the bilateral talks. According to Yin Rugeng after the meeting, the important matter discussed between the two parties this month was the issue of exchanging garrisons for the newly formed Special Police Force in the war zone, which has generally made progress. It is believed that it will be possible to enter the area within a short period of time. The principle of taking over the Eastern Mausoleum of Malanyu had already been agreed upon, but there were some difficulties in implementation. The discussion today focused on this point. However, the date of the takeover has not yet been determined. I will leave Tianjin and return within a day or two. According to Tao Shangming, the number of guns and personnel that the Special Police Force in the war zone should carry when entering Luandong to exchange garrisons had already been discussed and there were no problems. It will be implemented soon. The atmosphere of drugs in Tangdong and other places has been cracked down by 60% to 70% through successive negotiations. It is expected to be completely eliminated soon. This matter was also studied today to find a way to facilitate its implementation. The political situation in Luandong is still stable. I will return to Tangshan in a day or two.

Doihara arrived in Tianjin from Ping at 7:00 PM on the 9th. Sakai, the chief of staff of the Japanese army in Tianjin, and senior staff officers Oki and Kawaguchi all went to the station to welcome him. After Doihara got off the train, he went to the Tokiwa Inn in the Japanese Concession. That evening, Meijin, the commander of the Japanese garrison, hosted him at the Haiguang Temple barracks, accompanied by Sakai and Japanese Consul-General Kawagoe. At around 10:00 AM on the 10th, Doihara and Oki visited Yu Xuezhong at the Zhili Provincial Government and left after talking for about an hour. At 11:00 AM on the 11th, he visited Mayor Zhang Tingao at the Municipal Government and talked for about half an hour. He described his feelings about coming to China and stated that he had no mission, saying that the relations between China and Japan had deteriorated due to the deadlock in the China-Japan issue. This time, he plans to visit various places and meet with various authorities to show contact and to hear the opinions of the Chinese authorities on how to restore Sino-Japanese friendship and maintain East Asian peace. He recently heard that the Chinese government has banned the transportation of salt to Japan. He did not know the truth of the matter. Zhang told him that the reason why salt was not transported to Japan was because the transportation cost was too high. After arriving in Japan, the price was very low. All the salt merchants automatically did not transport it, and the government did not issue any orders to prohibit it. That evening at 7:00 PM, Zhang hosted a banquet at the Municipal Government. Doihara is scheduled to go to Qingdao on the 12th and then go south to Shanghai. (11th)
