Decline of the Guangdong Match Industry 96

Five Large Factories Closed Down Last Year

Remaining Factories Have Not Resumed Work This Spring

Guangzhou Correspondence: The Guangdong match industry, at its peak, had more than a hundred match factories in various places. After 1924, the workers demanded a wage increase and won. The wage increase dealt a blow to the business. In addition, the commercial recession in the Nanyang region in recent years has greatly reduced the sales of Guangdong matches to the Nanyang market. By 1932, only about 30 factories remained. The industry was barely surviving. The reason why it could not compete with foreign goods in the Nanyang market was that the cost of Guangdong-made matches was too high. It was found that the wages for Guangdong-made matches were high, and after leaving the factory, they had to pay two taxes. That is, each gross (1,200 boxes) of matches had to pay a unified tax of 3.8 yuan and a raw material tax of 1 yuan. Including the cost, the selling price of each gross was about 8 yuan. On the other hand, foreign matches were almost one-third cheaper per gross. Therefore, foreign matches not only occupied the entire Nanyang market, but even in the inland areas, imported matches were transported and sold. As a result, the Guangdong match industry was on the verge of collapse. Last year, due to the lack of sales of goods, the factories had an inventory of matches worth about 2 million yuan. Moreover, during the year-end period, there was no cash turnover, so the factories stopped production at the end of the year. Those who were unable to support and declared bankruptcy included Guangzhou Gongyi Factory, Jiangmen Wenming Factory, Huadi Dayi Factory, Shiqiao Guangzhongxing Factory, and Taishan Zhujiang Factory, totaling five factories. The loss of capital reached more than 1 million yuan, which caused a great impact. As for those who stopped production but did not go bankrupt, there is still no hope of resuming production since the spring. It is heard that the goods accumulated last year have not been sold off yet. If the sales gradually increase in the spring and the inventory is gradually sold off, the factories will be able to resume production three months later. Otherwise, the future is unimaginable. According to investigations, there are currently only eleven match factories remaining in the province, including China, Guangda, Dongshan, Guangdong, and Qiaoming branches in Guangzhou, Qiaoming and Guangzhou factories in Foshan, Xinan Factory in Sanshui, Minsheng Factory in Nanhai, Guangming Factory in Jiangmen, and Minxing Factory in Qingyuan. The above eleven factories have more than 100,000 long-term workers and 70,000 to 80,000 temporary employees. If there is no way to resume production for a while, more than 100,000 workers will lose their jobs. The Match Industry Union has been holding meetings in recent days to discuss ways to maintain the industry and has convened representatives from both labor and capital. The capital side has proposed to cancel the wage increase conditions for the labor side in 1924 in order to maintain the business, but it has not yet been agreed to by the labor side. Based on this speculation, there is still no definite date for the factories to resume production. (February 10th)

Zhu Jiahua's Speech on Transportation 97

Beijing News: Minister of Transportation Zhu Jiahua delivered a speech at the Central Broadcasting Station at 6:00 PM today (the 15th) on "Transportation Projects Underway This Year." The original text is recorded as follows:

The Central Broadcasting Station asked me to speak on the general situation of China's transportation industry last year, but only today did I have the time. I came to the Ministry of Transportation in the winter of the 21st year and believed that the transportation industry has a great relationship with the survival of the country and the lives of the people. Naturally, a conservative or downsizing policy cannot be adopted, but due to economic relations, we had to first find a way to maintain the status quo. Therefore, we started by reorganizing the internal affairs, such as rectifying the discipline of employees, implementing independent accounting, unifying the internal affairs of telecommunications, and establishing the foundation for the merger of postal and telecommunications services. We also abolished the shipping administration registration office, tightened up various postal and telecommunications agencies and the China Merchants Bureau, and the personnel administration of the Eurasia and China Airlines, etc., so that various businesses were commercialized, and administrative supervision was made strict and rapid, so as to gradually develop national undertakings. The difficulties in the postal service have now passed, and internal discipline has gradually recovered. The final accounts for the 22nd year even had a surplus of more than 1.2 million yuan. If the funds allocated to civil aviation are also included, it will be more than this amount. Compared with the heyday of the postal service in the past, it is no less inferior. However, the previous losses still have to be gradually made up. After the private postal offices were banned, the postal service has been truly unified from now on. In the field of telecommunications, a rough outline has also been sorted out in the past two years, and there has also been considerable progress. However, the economic foundation was originally too poor. Although all the old debts, large and small, have now been sorted out, because we also have to bear the principal and interest of repaying the old debts, there is currently no surplus to engage in larger expansions. As for the China Merchants Bureau in the field of shipping administration, the business performance has improved relatively, but due to various reasons, there are still many difficulties at present. In the field of civil aviation, Eurasia and China Airlines have expanded routes and economized expenses, and have even reached the point of suitable income and expenditure. China Airlines is now seeing improvement day by day. Now, at the beginning of the 24th year, let me briefly talk about the undertakings that are planned to be undertaken this year. At the same time, in order to understand the course of events, I cannot help but mention the past.

(A) Postal Service

The development of the postal service actually cannot but depend on the development of other transportation tools such as railways, highways, automobiles, and ships. However, as far as the postal service itself is concerned, China has a considerable foundation. The resolutions passed at the postal conference in September last year will continue to be implemented separately in the future. As for the more important matters to be carried out this year, (1) reorganize postal districts and expand the powers of the management bureau. The original postal districts were divided according to the previous transportation, political, and economic situation, which did not conform to the administrative regions very well. Now, because of the development of transportation undertakings such as highways, trains, aviation, telegraphs, and telephones, and the necessity of being consistent with the telecommunications districts after the merger of postal and telecommunications services last year, it is necessary to re-divide the postal districts. For example, the postal districts of Jiangsu and Anhui are vast, which is inconvenient. In terms of powers, because the postal business was not developed in the past, even an expenditure of several yuan had to be submitted to the Director of Postal Services of the General Post Office for approval, which could not give full play to its ability, and the General Post Office often reviewed it without understanding the local situation and needs, which had an impact on the development of the postal service. Now, regulations are being formulated to increase the responsibilities of the management bureau, so that ordinary events can be resolved on the spot, and events within the jurisdiction area should also be planned by them first, so that the General Post Office can concentrate on the responsibility of supervision and command, and will not be distracted by trivial matters. (2) Promote the postal service in the inland provinces and add bureaus and offices. The equipment in the inland bureaus and offices is still very simple, and there are still counties, townships, and towns that have not yet been opened to postal services, which should be reorganized or expanded separately. After all the private postal offices were closed at the end of last year, the postal administration bureaus of various provinces have added many third-class bureaus and agency offices in the inland, and they also deliver mail to places where no bureaus or offices have been set up for free. However, postal routes should still be opened up and bureaus and offices should be added. (3) Expand postal routes in border provinces. The establishment of bureaus and offices by the postal service has always been based on the principle of whether income and expenditure can be balanced. However, for the sake of developing the people's wisdom and culture in remote provinces, we should open up postal routes regardless of losses or strive for their development. For example, the postal affairs of Xikang are now being handled by personnel sent by the Sichuan Postal Administration Bureau. In the future, a management bureau or a first-class bureau will be set up in Kangding or Batang, directly under the Postal Administration Bureau. On the one hand, we will find ways to promote the entire postal service in Tibet. In the future, a management bureau must also be established in Lhasa. This matter is being discussed with the local authorities in Tibet, and it may be realized in a few months. Also, Qinghai is very vast, so a management bureau or a first-class bureau must also be established in Xining. (4) Build post office buildings. There are more than 2,300 post offices in the country (not including more than 10,000 agency offices). Only more than 80 of them have their own real estate. The others are rented private houses, which are not suitable. Therefore, we started to proceed with the design and construction of bureau houses in Nanchang, Changsha, Wuchang, Chengdu, Wuhu, Zhengzhou, Jiujiang, Shashi, Batang, Xining, and other important locations last year, and they will be completed in order. (5) The use of postal savings. Postal savings were more than 18 million yuan in the winter of the 21st year. The highest record before was more than 21 million yuan. Last year, due to the difficulty of safe investment, efforts were made to restrict it, and several provinces and regions stopped accepting savings. Now, the total has increased to more than 37 million yuan. At the same time, due to economic instability, for the benefit of depositors, investment has been specially restricted since the year before last, and large amounts of money have been deposited in reputable major banks, and a portion of the cash has been stored in the treasury. Therefore, the postal savings were not affected in the slightest by the financial crisis. However, this kind of savings comes from the people in various places and should not be used exclusively in urban areas. Therefore, we are now paying special attention to rural loans, so as to benefit farmers and ensure that loans are safe. Last year, the Hunan Post Office used a certain amount of money to be responsible for lending to rural areas by the bank. This year, we will try it out in several places. (6) Preparing for remittance of savings. The basic method of remittance of savings is that all deposits can be used to open a remittance account, and the post office will assign a number in turn. No matter who is in a general savings place, they can hand over the money to the post office and transfer it to the designated number. The China Post Office will notify the account holder of the number to withdraw it at any time, or ask for the deposit book to be recorded. Each time the remittance is taken, the job is clean, and merchants feel convenient. If both parties have this savings, they can hold the book and request direct remittance, one out and one in, without having to pay in cash, which is even more convenient. This method is available in various countries. The Ministry has also ordered preparations for it again and again last year. However, China's currency is not very uniform, and the market is different, so it is difficult to handle. However, preparations have been largely completed, and this year, it will be piloted in the six postal districts of Zhejiang, Jiangsu, Anhui, Shandong, Hebei, Beiping, and Shanghai, so as to gradually promote it. (7) Preparing for simple life insurance. The simple life insurance system can provide a considerable guarantee for the lives of poor people, and at the same time cultivate the habit of saving. The collected funds can be used to invest in local public utilities, directly and indirectly benefiting the society—especially the general public. Various countries have been running it for a long time, some are run by merchants, and some are run by post offices. Japan is quite developed, and it is run by the post office. The maximum amount of insurance is 450 yuan. At present, the total amount received is said to be more than 20 million yuan, and the national society has benefited greatly. The Ministry has drafted a plan, which is now being reviewed by the Legislative Yuan, and will be announced soon. The maximum amount of insurance is tentatively set at 900 yuan. Personnel who will handle this postal service will be trained next month. This year, it will be piloted in Nanjing and Shanghai first, and then gradually promoted. (8) Post offices purchase books, newspapers, and magazines on behalf of others. In order to subsidize cultural undertakings and facilitate the purchase of books and newspapers by people in various places, the Ministry formulated regulations and compiled a general catalog of books across the country last year. Post offices in various places have started purchasing on behalf of others from April last year and January this year. Because the publishing industry in China is not well organized, each publishing house publishes its own books, and the remittance procedures are cumbersome, which is especially inconvenient for people in the inland, which hinders the development of culture a lot. Now, it is extremely convenient to promote it through the post office, and it should be improved at any time in the future. (9) Drawing postal maps. The third edition of the postal map issued at the end of the year before last was revised based on the previous map. All the routes of ships, railways, automobiles, aviation, and telegraphs are recorded in more detail than before. However, in the past, postal maps were drawn by postal staff, focusing on the records of bureaus, offices, and lines. As for the terrain and humanities, everything was omitted, and there were inevitably errors. Also, some postal wall maps were drawn in the 10th year of the Republic of China and are no longer very suitable. Last year, the Ministry sent experts to the General Post Office to sort them out and redraw them, and asked the Land Survey Bureau and the Geographical Society to assist in the work. It is expected that they can be printed in about June or July. (10) Population survey. Post offices in China have always paid attention to the handling of population surveys and have published reports. Last year, statistical staff were sent to the General Post Office to plan properly and continue to handle them. It will be completed this autumn.

(B) Telecommunications

Telecommunications has also made considerable progress. The average monthly income of international radio was 150,000 yuan in the 21st year, and it increased to 330,000 yuan in the 23rd year. The average monthly income of the Shanghai Telegraph Bureau is about 60,000 yuan. Together with the monthly income of 40,000 yuan from the Shanghai domestic radio station, it is 100,000 yuan per month. Now, it has increased to 170,000 yuan, and old materials, old machines, old poles, and old machines are being repaired and utilized as much as possible. Although the telecommunications equipment has been improved in many ways, it is still far from being completely modernized. Many cases were resolved at the telecommunications conference held in September last year, and they have been implemented in order. The matters to be realized this year are: (1) Complete the national important long-distance telephone trunk line. Since the establishment of the National Government, many provinces have been handling long-distance telephones. The opinions between the Ministry and the provinces often cannot be consistent. Therefore, we are now formulating measures to entrust the provincial governments to handle long-distance telephones on behalf of the Ministry, so that the business can be easily developed, and the national and provincial businesses will not conflict, so as to maintain the entire system of national long-distance telephones, and the economy will also be rational, so that long-distance telephones and wired telegraphs can be integrated. On the one hand, we will first determine the long-distance telephone trunk line plan for the nine provinces, so as to connect the telephone calls of the provinces. Last year, we successively completed the fund-raising and material purchase, etc. Now, it has been started, and most of it can be completed by the end of the year. It is also planned to extend the original plan to Xi'an, Taiyuan, and Lanzhou, so as to facilitate the transportation in the Northwest. In this plan, there was originally another project to expand the long-distance telephone network in Jiangsu Province. Later, some of the materials were transferred to Jiangxi and Fujian provinces. This year, the long-distance telephone network in these two provinces should be able to be completed in its entirety. In addition, it is planned to lay branch lines in Anhui and Henan provinces to complete the communication network. Now, long-distance telephones are being built between Wanxian and Chongqing, and wireless telephone stations are being built between Hankou and Chongqing. (2) Expansion of international radio stations. Since the winter of the 19th year, the business of international radio stations has been booming. Last year and in January this year, the three routes of China-UK, China-Japan, and China-Italy were opened successively, and the telegraph business was particularly prosperous. This year, we plan to negotiate with the telecommunications authorities of India, Australia, and Canada to open direct circuits. Therefore, in addition to the transceivers, there are also many international telegraphs in Tianjin, Qingdao, and Hankou. It is also planned to set up automatic telegraph stations with lower power to communicate directly with neighboring places, such as Japan, the Philippines, and Annam. Thirteen 3.5-kilowatt transceivers have been purchased and installed in various places. On the one hand, they can communicate international telegraph business, and on the other hand, they can supplement the speed of domestic telegraph transmission. International wireless telephones have also been tested and will be put into commercial use in the past two years. The Ministry has set up a machine at the Shanghai International Radio Station to test the telephone calls with various countries in Europe and the United States, and the results are good. Because the secret machine and terminal machine have not arrived, it has not been officially opened. It can be completed this summer, and it is planned to install several smaller telephone stations to communicate with neighboring countries. At the same time, it is planned to install a wireless telephone station in Guangzhou, Tianjin, and Hankou. It should be able to communicate in May, so as to connect with long-distance telephones and city telephones in various places, and can be transferred to foreign countries from Shanghai. The Guangzhou telephone station is run by the Ministry. When it is completed in the future, Hong Kong and Shanghai can also communicate. It is also planned to install 12 wireless telephone stations in the inland and remote important locations to complete the initial completion of the national telephone network. (3) Reorganization of city telephones. City telephones have now been retrofitted with automatic machines in major cities such as Beijing, Shanghai, Tianjin, Hankou, and Qingdao. As for the telephone bureaus in Suzhou, Zhenjiang, etc., the Nanchang Telephone Bureau, which was established last year, and the Xi'an Telephone Bureau, which is under construction, will all repair and apply the original manual machines in order to save costs. We are currently negotiating and expanding the Lanzhou and Yichang Telephone Bureaus, and plan to convert the Yantai and Wuhu Bureaus into common-battery type and expand them. The Chengdu Telephone Bureau will also be taken back, and we will start to add 1,000 common-battery type telephones. In addition, small magneto-type bureaus, such as Dongtai, Anyang, and Huaiyin, are being carried out successively and must be completed uniformly this year. (4) Improvement of telegraph business. In the past two years, trunk lines have been repaired more and machines in large bureaus have been replaced more. This year, it is planned to reorganize the branch lines and machines in small bureaus, and promote public telegraph ciphers, using one word to replace one word or one sentence, so as to reduce the number of words. For meteorological telegraphs, we will also consult with relevant agencies to reorganize them to ensure that they are fast and accurate. After the promulgation of the National Phonetic Telegraph, it has not been promoted, and the National Phonetic Standard has also been changed. In the past two years, the Ministry has compiled the National Phonetic Telegraph and recompiled it according to the new standard. It can be completed and promoted this year. (5) Expansion of the repair factory. The Ministry's Telecommunications Material Repair Factory has been established in Nanjing since last year and has now taken shape. This year, it is planned to expand it. We are now investigating the needs of telecommunications materials across the country, including those for military use, so as to gradually expand it. (6) Training of personnel. The Telecommunications School was suspended because it was not run properly. In addition, nearly 300 people have been dismissed or retired due to cases involving telegraph service personnel. Recently, the business has been gradually promoted, and the city telephones and long-distance telephones that have been taken back and newly established have increased day by day, and the demand for personnel has also increased. In the future, when the long-distance telephone business in the nine provinces is completed, the telephone service personnel must be technically trained in advance. Therefore, a training institute will be established in Beijing this year. On the one hand, we will transfer existing personnel from various places in batches for further training, and on the other hand, we will recruit qualified personnel. (7) Conducting publicity. The telecommunications agencies of the Ministry have complete equipment and convenient communication. Now, we plan to publicize transportation undertakings and pay attention to social and commercial news. We will also pay attention to international publicity. At the same time, we plan to set up broadcasting stations in major ports. The 10-kilowatt broadcasting station in Shanghai can be completed this summer. We are now planning the entire national broadcasting network. This matter is of great importance to education and cultural undertakings. We have also started to deal with the chaotic situation of various broadcasting stations in Shanghai, and the Wireless Radio Design Committee will be established in the shortest possible time to maintain the domestic spatial order and allocate broadcasting stations across the country into a complete plan. (To be continued)

Establishment of the Wuhan Federation of Trade Unions 98

The First Congress of Representatives Held

Liu Hanqing and Others Elected as Directors and Supervisors

Wuhan News: The Wuhan Federation of Trade Unions has not been established yet. Last year, Chairman Chiang visited Wuhan and ordered the establishment of the Trade Union Consolidation Committee, which was responsible for the consolidation by five agencies, including the General Headquarters, and the consolidation was to be completed within six months. This morning (the 15th), the city's workers held the first congress of representatives. Forty-one units of industrial and occupational trade unions sent representatives, with a total of 1,547 representatives. The Central People's Movement Committee, the General Headquarters, the Pacification Commissioner's Office, the Provincial Government, the Municipal Party Department, and the Municipal Government all sent personnel to supervise and guide the election. Liu Hanqing, Li Renzhu, Jiang Boxiong, Chen Jian, Qin Jie, Ren Hanchen, Yang Wenqi, Zhou Wenqing, Tian Yadan, Yin Zichao, and Neng Bin and other eleven people were publicly elected as the presidium, with Liu Hanqing as the chairman, who reported on the preparation process. Li Renzhu, the supervisor of the election from the Central People's Movement Committee, Zhang Fubao, the supervisor of the election from the General Headquarters, Liu Yaping, the supervisor of the election from the Pacification Commissioner's Office, Yun Ji, the supervisor of the election from the Provincial Government, Cui Zixin, the instructor from the Municipal Party Department, and Xu Wenguang, the instructor from the Municipal Government, made speeches in succession. After the chairman delivered a reply, the proposals were discussed and resolved: (1) Send a telegram to support Chairman Chiang in wiping out the remaining Red bandits and to comfort the soldiers at the front. (2) Petition the Central Government and the Chairman's Headquarters to provide relief for the expenses of the Wuhan trade union during the five-province bandit suppression period, so as to facilitate the work. (3) Send a telegram to trade unions across the country to work together to promote production and build economic national defense. (4) Submit a report to the Provincial and Municipal Governments and forward it to the Ministry of Industry of the Executive Yuan to severely crack down on the cotton yarn exchange. (5) The provisions of Article 20 of the Trade Union Law are contrary to the Party's purpose of organizing and training the people. Petition the Central Government to issue an order to amend it. (6) The stack workers in Qiaokou encroached on the sewing and packaging work, endangering the livelihood of the workers, and the matter was handed over to the board of directors and supervisors for handling. In the afternoon, the directors and supervisors were elected. Nine directors were elected: Liu Hanqing, Ren Hanchen, Du Xianda, Qin Jie, Yin Lei, Chen Jian, Yang Hao, Han Zhen, and Hu Yuanshou. Five supervisors were elected: Tian Yadan, Li Renzhu, Shi Jinghou, Chen Wenju, and Li Jiru. The swearing-in ceremony of the directors and supervisors will be held at a later date. (15th)

Zhejiang Province's Work Relief Road Construction 99

To Start Within This Month

Quzhou News: The work relief in this province was planned by the Construction Department last year, and the approved funding was 3 million yuan, with 1 million yuan for water conservancy, 600,000 yuan for road construction, and 400,000 yuan for agricultural improvement. The work relief funds for water conservancy and agricultural affairs have been determined by the competent department of the Construction Department for their use and distribution. As for the road construction, the work relief road construction is currently being surveyed. The Tongfen, Sanmen Bay branch line, and Anxiao and Jiaping and other five roads have been approved by the provincial government for implementation. The lengths of the five highways are: (1) Linhai to Xianju line, 15 kilometers; (2) Sanmen Bay branch line, 25.5 kilometers; (3) Linping to Jiaxing line, 95 kilometers; (4) Tonglu to Fenshui line, 42 kilometers; (5) Jiaxing to Huzhou line, 58.3 kilometers, totaling 265 kilometers. It is estimated that 2.78 million yuan will be needed for road construction. As of last month, the above five roads had not yet started construction because the contractors were all waiting to see if all the construction funds would be paid before they would agree to undertake the construction. Other work relief roads will also have to wait until the survey of these five roads is completed before they can continue to be handled. However, the recruitment of workers and road construction can only build the roadbed earthwork project. The pavement, bridge, and culvert projects still need to be contracted out. According to the Road Bureau, this work relief road construction is expected to start this month. (10th)

Songjiang 100

Two Prisoners Die Tragically in Prison

Zhao A'mei, a woman from Shihudang Township, was 21 years old. Last year, she went to Zhang's recommendation shop in Fuxiatang and was recommended to work as a servant in a certain family. Later, because Zhang demanded payment without success, he detained Zhao's clothes and bags, and a quarrel broke out. Then Zhang beat Zhao, who then bit off Zhang's finger. The case was reported to the Public Security Bureau and transferred to the court. As a result, Zhao was sentenced to one year and two months in prison. However, Zhao was young and inexperienced. After entering prison, her injuries flared up, and her appearance gradually became haggard. Three months ago, she was coughing up blood and bedridden. Her family was poor and never came to visit her. She died in prison yesterday. After the inspection, she was put in a coffin for burial. Everyone who heard about it was saddened.

Also, Zhu Ziying and Diao Zizong from Xuzhou pretended to be members of the Public Security Bureau and extorted cigarette money from the Chen family's small teahouse in Chenjiaxing, Zhujingbang Township, in the name of catching gambling. The owner of the teahouse saw through them and turned them over to the nearby Public Security Bureau. They were transferred to the court, and Zhu was sentenced to two months in prison and Diao to 40 days in prison. It was reported that Zhu's old illness recurred and he died yesterday. After the judge's inspection, he was also put in a coffin for burial.

Suzhou 101

Wang Baofa Beats His Wife to Death

Yang, the wife of Wang Baofa, a resident of Zhouzhuang Township, was cooking in the kitchen the night before last (the 14th) when the couple had a quarrel. Baofa became angry for a while and took a hard wooden stick and hit Yang's head hard, hitting the vital point. She died of serious injuries on the morning of the 15th. When Officer Hong of the Sixth First Branch of the Public Security Bureau heard the news, he immediately arrested Wang on suspicion of beating his wife to death. He also sent a letter to the local court. Yesterday (the 16th), Prosecutor Shen took a steamboat to the countryside for inspection.

Wuxi 102

Ministry of Communications Expands Long-Distance Telephone Lines

The Ministry of Communications, in view of the increasing improvement of domestic construction and the gradual completion of highway construction, believes that it is necessary to add more lines in various places and has ordered its subordinates to make preparations. It is learned that the Minhang Branch of the Shanghai Telephone Bureau was established on February 6 and started telephone service. Minhang, Beiqiao, Zhuanqiao, Hupu, and Fushan also started telephone service on the 5th. The Liyang Long-Distance Telephone Business Office has been prepared and started telephone service on February 1. Telephones east of Wuxi are connected and transferred through Yixing, and Wuxi West Mountain Wujin Yixing connects and transfers. After the establishment of the Hushuguan Branch of the Wuxian Telegraph Bureau, it started business on February 1. A telegraph and telephone office was established in Xinzhen, a place between Kunshan and Taicang, on January 30 and started telephone service. The Danyang Long-Distance Telephone Office believes that the telephone service time at night is very short and there is only one telephone operator. It has specially petitioned the Ministry of Communications to stipulate the business hours. If there are air defense telephones and express telephones, they can be connected and transferred at any time. It has been tentatively decided that the telephone service hours for Danyang, Longtan, Taicang, and Kunshan will be from 7:00 AM to 12:00 PM every day. In addition to the original provincial long-distance telephone line between Wuxi, the Ministry of Communications will also hang a pair of phantom lines on the Beijing-Hangzhou Highway, which is expected to be connected to telephone service in March. The direct line of the Beijing-Hangzhou Road has been connected to telephone service on February 1.

Shell Explodes and Injures Two People

Zhang Shunxing Iron Shop outside Nanmen was opened by Zhang Renquan and is doing good business. Recently, the shop took in a batch of iron shells, about one foot long. Yesterday (the 16th) at about 8:00 AM, Zhang Renquan and his apprentice Zhou Fuxiang put the shells into the coal stove, preparing to transform them into other objects. Unexpectedly, the shell leaves were heated and suddenly exploded. With a loud bang, the roof tiles moved, and shrapnel flew everywhere. The shell pierced through the back wall and fell into the river. Zhang and Zhou were seriously injured in the face and other places and have been sent to Puren Hospital for treatment. It is said that their lives may be in danger. After the Third Branch of the Public Security Bureau heard the news, it immediately sent police to investigate and reported it to the General Department for verification.

Jiangyin 103

Huangtiangang Canal Dredging is Scheduled

The dredging of the South Canal of Huangtiangang is being actively carried out. The Construction Department sent engineer Yu Dejie and engineer Wu Xuexun to Cheng on the 14th, and the engineering office was established on the 15th and started working. It was decided to notify ships in various counties of Jiangsu Province from the 20th that they are not allowed to enter the port to facilitate the disconnection of the venue. Regarding the dredging cost budget, it is estimated that the total length from the mouth of Huangtiangang to Qingzhen is 26.85 kilometers, and the amount of excavated soil is about 793,000 cubic meters, which is divided into two types: machine excavation and manual excavation. The amount of soil excavated manually is about 700,000 cubic meters, which requires 7,100 coolies and workers to engage in excavation. The total cost is 160,000 yuan, which is allowed to be used from the 50,000 yuan of the Shu Yanzhen Wuyun River project account and the 15,000 yuan of the project account subsidized by the provincial government as resolved by the provincial government. The remaining 95,000 yuan will be borrowed from the local government and used as a ship donation for offsetting. Yesterday (the 14th), Magistrate Yan of the Mountain County, together with Chen Zhisan and Liu Chiying of the Farmers Bank of China, and Chairman Wu Shuying of the Chamber of Commerce, went to Wuxi to borrow money from the China Shanghai Banks. The result was good. The Construction Department also instructed the county government that the method of offsetting the borrowed cash is feasible in principle. However, the third item, the request to allocate a new public bond of 50,000 yuan for borrowing, should be transferred to the Water Conservancy Construction Public Bond Supervision and Use Committee of this province for review, and Magistrate Yan was appointed as the deputy director of the project account office, responsible for handling it.

Danyang 104

Former Agricultural Bank Director Zhang Hanlin Sentenced

Zhang Hanlin, the former director of the local Farmers Bank, was repeatedly summoned by the county government for embezzlement and fraud during his tenure, as well as colluding with Yin Xin of the Miaoduan Cooperative to accept bribes, and finally sentenced. Zhang Hanlin was sentenced to two years and six months imprisonment and fined one thousand yuan for continuously embezzling items held in the course of his duties with the intention of illegally possessing them for himself. He was also sentenced to two years and six months imprisonment and fined five hundred yuan for repeatedly demanding and accepting bribes in the course of his duties. The combined sentence is three years and six months imprisonment, a fine of one thousand two hundred yuan, and deprivation of civil rights for two years. Yin Xin was sentenced to one year imprisonment and a fine of one hundred yuan for helping Zhang Hanlin repeatedly demand and accept bribes in the course of his duties.

Changshu 105

Victim Fights Robbers, Both Sides Injured

The Huangni Bridge area in the Third District, close to the lake marshlands, has many bandits. The family of Zhang Abing, a farmer in that area, is relatively well-off. Unexpectedly, they were robbed. The victim, Zhang, seeing that the robbers were mostly unarmed, fought back. Unfortunately, it was late at night and there was a lack of assistance, and the robbers relied on their numbers. Zhang Abing and his son, Jinsheng, were both severely beaten, their heads broken and bleeding. The robbers then searched and looted miscellaneous items, taking everything, totaling a loss of approximately seven to eight hundred yuan. On the 15th, the two victims came to the city to seek treatment at the county hospital and reported the robbery to the county police.

Nantong 106

Sword Mountain Murder Case Opens

A cruel rape and murder case occurred at the foot of Jianshan Mountain in the south of Nantong city. The case involves a farmer, Fan Hengyu, whose wife, Miss Sun Fen, had an affair with a neighbor, He Hei. The adulterer and adulteress colluded to murder Fan Hengyu, stabbing him eleven times and dumping his body in the river. The Public Security Bureau arrested the male and female perpetrators and handed them over to the court. The prosecutor filed a public indictment. On the 15th, Judge Shao of the criminal court opened the trial. The two perpetrators continued to argue, but after witnesses testified and the police found the bloody clothes as evidence, they finally bowed their heads in silence. The court ordered them to be remanded in custody.

Xiaoshan 107

Large Number of Shops Announce Closure

Shops in various industries inside and outside the county town have been affected by last year's drought. No fewer than dozens of them closed down at the end of the lunar year. For example, the century-old Jiuda Native Goods Store in the West Market, the Fusunxing Native Goods Store in the East Market, as well as the Lingxing Native Goods Store, the Songsheng Calico Store, the Yuantai Native Goods Store, the Yao Fumao Rice Store, and the Yongsheng Oil and Candle Store along Changbang have all announced their closure and are settling their accounts. The economic depression in commerce is evident.

Local News

Financial Advisory Committee Established Yesterday 108

First Meeting Held, Deputy Chairman and Committee Members Appointed

Central News Agency reports: The Financial Advisory Committee held its first meeting yesterday afternoon at Minister Kong's private residence. The committee members present were Minister Kong, Zhang Gongquan, Chen Xing, Tang Shumin, Li Fusun, Chen Guangfu, Qian Xinzhi, Hu Bijang, Xu Xinliu, Ju Songsun, Xu Kan, Song Ziliang, Xi Demao, Qin Runqing, Chen Zheqing, Qian Changzhao, Shen Shuyu, Wu Yunzhai, and Ye Fuxiao. After the meeting began as scheduled, Minister Kong delivered an opening speech, saying that today is the day of the establishment of the Financial Advisory Committee, and he has endless thoughts and hopes. The current Chinese economy and finance do have many difficult problems. In essence, these difficult problems mostly arise from the lack of a sound foundation in China's economy and finance. The public must think that this committee will solve many of the current problems. However, his purpose is to hope that everyone will use their accumulated experience and intellect to jointly study and build a sound economic foundation for China. However, everyone is very busy and sacrifices their precious time, which he feels ashamed of. Because China's economic organization does not have a sound foundation, any novel foreign policies, which sound very appealing, will inevitably be unsuitable once implemented. Therefore, any plan to remedy China's economy and finance must be suitable for China's national conditions. Arbitrarily imitating others will not only be useless but may also increase difficulties. We must know that we are a backward country and must first do a lot of basic construction work before we can be on par with other countries. In other words, we should first maximize the development and utilization of our inherent resources to make the entire national economy deeply rooted. At the same time, we should base the economic construction plan on national habits and social development processes and adopt economic policies. Not only must we have a thorough understanding of the domestic situation, but we must also be well-versed in the trends of the world economy. Because today the economies of all countries in the world have close interrelationships. Everyone is a leader in the banking and business sectors and has a keen observation of domestic and foreign business conditions. In the future, this committee will be able to provide appropriate suggestions to the government's construction plans by considering both Chinese and foreign situations. The government will also humbly adopt them. Recently, the government officials in charge have repeatedly declared their financial policies: First, they will never lightly use superficial shortcuts to solve the basic problems of our country's current finance and economy. Second, they will never adopt extreme measures that would shake the people's credit and hinder the future of economic construction. At the same time, we should also recognize that there are areas for improvement in China's currency and financial organization. Now, domestic trade between producers and merchants in various regions is still unable to fully develop due to the lack of adequate financial regulation. Therefore, we must carefully improve the current issuance system to obtain a more unified, stable, and widely circulating currency. In addition, we should set up more financial institutions and agricultural warehouses in the inland, and implement bill discounting to make inland finance more active. There is also the matter of the government's great anxiety about our country's huge trade deficit. Although there is no way to remedy it in the short term, we must always actively find ways to gradually stabilize foreign trade. This committee should provide practical suggestions to meet the government's expectations. Therefore, the scope of work of this committee is very broad, and the responsibility entrusted to this committee by the government is very heavy. At the same time, the government is very grateful for everyone's loyal service. Then, the chairman, in accordance with the law, appointed Committee Member Zhang Gongquan as Deputy Chairman and appointed the committee members of each group. The first group includes Tang Shouliang, Chen Xing, Zhang Gongquan, Xu Kan, Qian Xinzhi, and Wu Daquan, with Tang Shumin as the director. The second group includes Bei Songsun, Xi Demao, Wu Yunzhai, and Shen Shuyu, with Bei Songsun as the director. The third group includes Li Fusun, Qian Changzhao, Song Ziliang, Xu Xinliu, and Ye Fuxiao, with Li Fusun as the director. The fourth group includes Chen Guangfu, Hu Bijang, Qin Runqing, Zhou Zuomin, Chen Zheqing, with Chen Guangfu as the director. Zhang Gongquan expressed his best efforts to serve as the vice chairman of the council. He hoped that the members of each group would focus on basic issues, conduct research and discussion, and contribute to the government. This council is an advisory body to the Ministry of Finance. Chairman Kong concurrently served as the Minister of Finance and the Governor of the Central Bank. Committee Member Xu Keting is the Director of the Currency Department. He hoped the committee relationship would bring the Ministry of Finance, the banking community, and society together to sincerely cooperate to overcome national difficulties. Then, Chairman Kong proposed that the National Federation of Commerce, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, and the Silver and Money Trade Association petitioned the Ministry of Finance to reward the import of foreign silver and exempt the new silver export tax added in October of the 23rd year when re-exporting. After discussion, it was deemed necessary to reward it. It was resolved that it could be approved, but it was still requested that the Ministry of Finance make a decision. Subsequently, Chairman Kong reported that the address of the committee would be attached to the Central Bank, and all secretarial affairs would be handled concurrently by the Secretariat of the Central Bank. Then the meeting adjourned.

Ambassador to Russia Yan Huiqing Scheduled to Return to His Post on the 20th 109

Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday Morning, Going to Hangzhou Tonight

Reception for Reporters in the Afternoon

New Voice News Agency reports: Dr. Yan Huiqing, our country's ambassador to Russia, returned to China and has been on vacation in the country for several months. He is now scheduled to leave Shanghai on the 20th of this month to return to his post. Mr. Yan arrived in Shanghai by train from Tianjin yesterday morning. He accepted the invitation of the Soviet Russian representative and is scheduled to leave Shanghai for Hangzhou tonight. After returning to Shanghai tomorrow, he will attend a tea party hosted by Minister Kong, Mayor Wu, and Minister Gu tomorrow night. Then he will go abroad with Mei Lanfang and others. Mr. Yan met with reporters yesterday and expressed his pleasure at returning to his post. The details are recorded as follows:

Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday Morning

Mr. Yan took the train from Tianjin southwards a few days ago, without any attendants. He did not stop when passing through Beijing the night before and came directly to Shanghai, arriving at the North Station at 8:20 yesterday morning. After getting off the train, he took a car directly to Room 345 on the 13th floor of the International Hotel on Jing'an Temple Road to rest. Those who welcomed him at the train station included Zhao Tiezhang, a representative of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs in Shanghai, Qian Xinzhi, General Manager of the Four Banks Savings Society, Yan Fuqing, President of the National Shanghai Medical College, and many relatives and friends.

Scheduled to Go to Russia

The "Northern" special ship sent by the Soviet Union to welcome Mr. Yan and the Mei's opera troupe left Vladivostok and headed south on the 8th, arriving in Shanghai on the morning of the 14th. After Mr. Yan arrived in Shanghai, he has decided to take the ship immediately without changing his plans. Now, he is only waiting for Mr. Mei Lanfang to finish the charity performance for the China Benevolent Childcare Association and the Jiangzhe Drought Relief Association and is scheduled to leave Shanghai on the 20th. It is estimated that it will take 25 to 26 days to reach Vladivostok, where he will transfer to a special Siberian railway train and arrive in Moscow before March 1st.

Accompanying Personnel

In addition to the Mei's opera troupe and Miss Hu Die and others who are going to Russia to attend the International Film Exhibition, those traveling to Russia with Mr. Yan include the newly appointed Third Secretary of the Embassy in the Soviet Union, Jiao Xiangzong, the former President of the Qingdao Physicians Association, attendant Wu Gang, the wife of the current Chargé d'Affaires in the Soviet Union Wu Nanru, Secretary Wei's wife, the wife of Xu Nianceng, the Consul-General in Khabarovsk, and the couple of Tian Kuanqi, the Vice Consul in Vladivostok.

Russian Consulate Banquet

Mr. Spilvanik, the Soviet Russian Consul-General and Chargé d'Affaires in Shanghai, welcomed Ambassador Yan and Mei Lanfang and others at the Soviet Russian Embassy office at No. 1 Huangpu Road at 12:30 yesterday afternoon. Mayor Wu Tiecheng, Secretary-General of the Executive Yuan Chu Minyi, Director of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs in Shanghai Yu Ming, Secretary-General of the Municipal Government Yu Hongjun, former Minister to France Chen Lu, and local celebrities Wang Xiaolai, Du Yuesheng, and Russian Vice Consul Zhurikovsky and others accompanied the banquet, which ended at around 2 pm.

Tea Party Tomorrow Night

Central dignitaries such as Minister of Finance Kong Xiangxi, Mayor Wu Tiecheng, Minister to France Gu Weijun, former Minister to France Chen Lu, Central Committee Member Cai Yuanpei, former Minister of Railways Ye Gongchao, Secretary-General of the Executive Yuan Chu Minyi, as well as Feng Gengguang, Du Yuesheng, Shen Shuyu, Yuan Ludeng, Huang Jinrong, Zhang Yin, Li Zhaohuan, Li Xuangong, Li Yuying, Yang Hu, Jin Tingsun, Lin Kanghou, Qian Yongming, Pan Gongzhan, Bei Zuyi, Xu Shiying, Chen Guangfu, Yu Ming, Xu Xinliu, Chen Qicai, Liu Zhanen, Zhang Zhuping, Wu Zaizhang, Zhang Shouyong, Wang Xiaolai, Ma Yinliang, Shen Kunshan, Zhao Zunyu, Zhang Jia'ao, Tang Shumin, Chen Jie, Li Denghui, Wang Boqi, Zhang Wenhuan, Xiong Xiling, Yu Zuoting, Hu Yun, Zhu Shaoping, Yu Qiaqing, Yu Hongjun, and more than forty others, have jointly invited Ambassador Yan, Mei Lanfang, and other related Chinese and Russian figures to a grand tea party at the International Hotel from 4:30 pm to 6:30 pm tomorrow to bid farewell to the two gentlemen.

Remarks

Mr. Yan met with reporters at the International Hotel yesterday afternoon. He said that he had been abroad for more than two years before, returned to China to take care of private affairs, and inspected the domestic situation. Later, due to physical discomfort, he was unable to return to his post earlier. Recently, his health has gradually recovered. He did not intend to return to his post, but considering that the resumption of diplomatic relations between China and Russia was entirely negotiated by him and Litvinov in the League of Nations, and that he was appointed as the first ambassador to Russia after the resumption of diplomatic relations for only a year or so, it would seem unreasonable to resign suddenly. At the same time, the government also found it difficult to find a successor for a while, and the embassy staff in the Soviet Union also hoped that he would return to his post. Therefore, he decided to return to his original post.

Close Diplomatic Relations

Mr. Yan continued that after the resumption of diplomatic relations between China and Russia, the exchanges between the two sides have been very close. Not only in culture, our country often has military, transportation, education, municipal, and military attaché groups going to inspect. In terms of commerce, it is also very progressive. He recently heard that the Soviet Union is now ordering 4,000 tons of Chinese tea, and the import of Russian coal, wood, and so on is also a good phenomenon in the diplomatic relations between the two countries. This time, Russia invited Mei Lanfang and others to perform, which will further promote the development of culture between China and Russia. Therefore, he feels quite happy about this trip. As for the Chinese tea merchants, he hopes that they can unite, which will be more powerful in international trade.

Sino-Russian Diplomacy

Regarding Sino-Russian diplomacy, Mr. Yan said that our country has always opposed the Middle East Railway issue and has repeatedly protested. The Sino-Russian Commercial Treaty is in progress in Beijing. It can continue after the Russian ambassador returns to his post.

International Situation

Mr. Yan finally said that Sheng Shicai, the administrator of Xinjiang, once invited him to go to Xinjiang, but it was not possible in reality. He plans to go there if he has the opportunity after arriving in Russia. Regarding Sino-Japanese relations and Hirota's speech, we need to see how things develop. Our country is a passive party in this matter, and Japan needs to be aware of it. The first step is to improve the atmosphere. Before the September 18th Incident, the two countries were very good. Therefore, to improve Sino-Japanese relations and not let them remain in a stalemate for a long time, we must first understand the cause and effect. As for Anglo-American cooperation, in terms of language, religion, economy, race, and history, there is a possibility, but the scope is too broad. The interests of the two countries in the Far East will of course be maintained. Even as the US ambassador stated, Britain's Far East policy has not changed, which means that it supports its consistent position. But we cannot hope to borrow others for assistance. This concept is indeed impossible and not what an independent country should have. Lord Lytton is an enthusiastic person, and his remarks are only to maintain the claims in his investigation report. Therefore, Mr. Li paid close attention to the affairs of Kwantung when he was in the UK to show that he always supported his report.

Sun Ke Discusses the Issue of Far Eastern Peace 110

Anglo-American Alliance Difficult to Realize

Sun Ke, the President of the Legislative Yuan, arrived in Shanghai by train the night before to bid farewell to Central Committee Member Wang Longhui, who is going abroad. Mr. Sun met with reporters from various newspapers at his private residence on Columbia Road yesterday morning. According to him, Mr. Wang Chonghui's task of running around the North and South of the country has been completed, and he is now returning to his post via Japan and the United States because his vacation is over. The collection of transaction taxes has precedents in various countries, but it is still a new tax in our country. Therefore, the tax rate is light. At present, the Regulations on Transaction Tax of the Exchange have been passed by the Legislative Yuan and will be implemented soon. Lord Lytton advocated the Anglo-American alliance to maintain peace in the Far East, but considering the facts, this statement is difficult to realize. The British Conservative Party recently advocated not to care about matters east of Singapore and to abandon the Singapore naval base to avoid war. The Labor Party advocates thorough peace, which is close to compromise. The attitude of the United States is also very ambiguous. From this point of view, it is difficult for Britain and the United States to unite to maintain peace in the Far East. However, if Britain and the United States continue to maintain the attitude of the past three years and hold the principle of seeking nothing, then within five years, Britain and the United States will have no foothold in the Far East.

March 22nd

The Great American Evening News reports: It was learned today (16th) that the Far East Commercial Investigation Group organized by the American Foreign Trade Association in New York will depart from San Francisco on a Dollar Company邮船 on March 22nd. This trip will pay special attention to China and will strive to promote the commercial relations between the United States and China and Japan. After arriving in Japan, they will stay for two weeks. Although Manchuria is not included in the itinerary, several members may separate from the main group and go for an informal investigation. Several other members may go south to Manila. After arriving in China, they will stay for six weeks or two months to conduct detailed investigations in various places to achieve the purpose of this trip. The current plan is to form the group with 15 to 25 important merchants, and several secretaries and experts will accompany them.

Minutes of the Annual Meeting of the American Chamber of Commerce 112

The China Press reports that the American Chamber of Commerce in Shanghai held its annual meeting yesterday (15th) at the American Community Center. Chairman Françoise briefly described the difficult period that the world, especially China, is currently going through. Last year, the American Chamber of Commerce requested the Chinese government to revise a certain clause of the Regulations on Encouraging Industry. The US Minister to China has received a notice stating that some modifications will be made. In addition, the troublesome clauses in the laws requiring goods imported into China to be labeled with the country of manufacture will also be relaxed. Furthermore, the certification of passport regulations, which is particularly inconvenient for those who go to the Philippines or Japan several times a year, is also under consideration for revision to give those who live in China the same treatment as Chinese living in the United States. One noteworthy item in the Chamber of Commerce's accounts last year was the relief work it carried out. The total amount used for relief, loans, and sending impoverished American expatriates back to their country throughout the year was 17,869 yuan and 81 cents. After the description, the members voted to approve the amendments to the charter proposed by the special committee. The main amendment was to increase the number of directors from 11 to 15. All the clauses were unanimously passed by the entire meeting. Then, Francoise and 14 others were elected as the new directors. Next, Frischman of the Shanghai Telephone Company stated that the company recently submitted a request to the工部局 to increase telephone charges, which is only to fulfill the contract signed three times before. In the past three years, the company's income has not been able to cover its expenses, so it feels that Shanghai users should fulfill that part of the contract. The new charter charges according to the number of calls, so the increased cost is borne by those who use the telephone more, and users in residential areas or those who use less water do not have to pay more. This method is very fair. Next, American Commercial Counselor Arnold detailed his observations on his return to the United States, saying that the people have mixed opinions on the new government, but in his personal opinion, things are indeed better than before. Next, he said that in order to increase the export trade of the United States, we must first seek to increase purchases, because buying and selling are mutually dependent. The extreme nationalism that has gradually expanded in recent years is no longer applicable today. As for the economic depression, he believes that the United States is now gradually approaching the period of turning from bad to good. Based on the statistics and other signs of 1934, he believes that it is now the time for the Chamber of Commerce to plan for development and strive to cooperate with Chinese and other countries. Next, he mentioned that the American Economic Investigation Group will depart from New York around March 18th to come to China. The members are all important figures in the business community and are very concerned about commercial issues here. After Arnold finished his speech, member Balenman suggested that a committee should be established to study China's export trade, but member Barsha said that this move is hopeless because the Chinese government never cares about exporters and often troubles merchants who try to increase China's export trade by imposing donations and increasing export taxes, even though the development of export trade can enable tens of millions of Chinese to obtain jobs and can bring new capital into China. However, the Chinese government does not regard encouraging this move as its task.

The Anti-Drug Conference Resolves Four Important Cases 114

The Chairman of the Chinese National Anti-Drug Association, Wang Yingqi, Vice Chairmen Li Denghui, Zhong Ketuo, General Manager Huang Jiahe, and others held a tea party yesterday at the 14th-floor restaurant of the International Grand Hotel on Jing'an Temple Road to entertain the association's committee members and anti-drug leaders. Over twenty people attended, including Xue Dubi, Chu Fucheng, Wu Kaisheng, Yin Zhufu, He Dekui, Liu Wang Liming, and Li Gongpu. Li Denghui and Zhong Ketuo successively gave speeches, briefly stating that the association's launch of the National Anti-Drug Movement has lasted over a decade. Its advocacy and undertakings have been witnessed by the people of the country. In recent years, due to environmental factors, the work has been slightly stagnant. Recently, the government has implemented a drug prohibition movement and a six-year eradication plan. The association should continue its efforts to jointly supervise and promote the complete eradication. They also expressed hope that all attendees would provide guidance on future plans and strategies. Huang Jiahe then reported on the association's recent work progress, and put forward ten proposals regarding the prohibition of opium. Chu Fucheng advocated that Shanghai, as a place of observation for both Chinese and foreigners, and also the center of opium, should be subject to the association's request to the authorities to strictly eradicate drugs to eliminate the root cause of the disaster. Subsequently, Wu Kaisheng, the former representative attending the International League of Nations Opium Suppression Conference, delivered a speech, briefly stating that the Chinese National Anti-Drug Association is the only anti-drug organization in China. Its past statements were bright and its advocacy was righteous, which was valued by the International League of Nations and various countries. All countries in the world know that China has this anti-drug association. In the past, for China's opium prohibition issues, many cited the association's proposals and reports as the basis. He himself, when attending the International Opium Suppression Conference in Europe, received a lot of help from the writings of the association's General Manager Huang, and other representatives also benefited from the association's documents. This shows the association's international status. In the future, they should unite comrades and provide spiritual and material support to expand its work, strive for opium prohibition, and win glory for the country. Xue Dubi gave a speech, briefly stating that he knew the association's work when he served in the northwestern provinces, and later, as Minister of Interior, he co-founded the Anti-Smoking Committee with the association's members, drafted the anti-smoking law, and deeply knew the association's deep relationship with China's opium prohibition. Currently, the government has announced a six-year eradication plan, and the association should request the government to implement it. Yin Zhufu then reported on his experience traveling to Shaanxi and praised the province's authorities for prohibiting the planting of opium and changing to planting cotton. He hoped that the province could persist to the end, extending from the first phase of 41 counties to the entire province, and that the association should work hard to promote its realization. Finally, the following resolutions were made: (1) Organize a Narcotics Research Committee; (2) Hold a grand anti-drug movement on June 3rd of this year, Lin Zexu Memorial Day; (3) Continue to publish the International Anti-Drug Newsletter; (4) Publicly elect Xue Dubi, Wang Jingqi, Chu Fucheng, Li Denghui, Zhong Ketuo, Wu Kaisheng, Huang Jiahe, and other seven people to revise the association's declaration on opium prohibition, and elect Huang Jiahe as the convener. The meeting adjourned after the discussion.

Huang Musong Arrived in Beijing Yesterday Morning 115

The Northwest Problem Research Association Gave a Farewell Banquet to Mr. Huang the Night Before

Huang Musong, the special envoy specially appointed by the Central Government to Tibet to pay tribute to the distant Dalai Lama, returned to China last winter via India and Nepal. He landed in Hong Kong at the beginning of this month, traveled to Guangdong for a short tour, and arrived in Shanghai from Hong Kong on the Changxing Company's Asia Queen ship the day before yesterday. He took the early train to Beijing at 8:00 yesterday morning to report everything to the Central Government. The Northwest Problem Research Association held a banquet to welcome Mr. Huang at the Banking Club on the fifth floor of the Bank Association at 6:00 the night before yesterday (the 15th). Over forty people attended, including Lin Kanghou, Chen Binhe, Pan Gongzhan, Yin Zhufu, Guo Weiping, Gao Changzhu, Wang Yuzhuang, Li Dachao, Pan Dajing, Wang Weisong, Dai Yuheng, Huang Jingwan, Ma Hongdao, Xu Zhaoxian, Li Shuqing, and Chen Yunsuan. First, Lin Kanghou delivered a welcome speech, briefly stating that Mr. Huang had worked hard for the country, traveled to the northwest, and provided a lot of support to the association. This time, he went to Tibet to pay tribute to the Dalai Lama, traveled for six or seven months, lasting a whole year. Although it was said to be full of hardships, it deepened the feelings between China and Tibet, completed the mission successfully, and returned with honor. This is the first reason why the association should express a warm welcome. Although the association's members are determined to study border affairs, it is difficult to obtain accurate information. Mr. Huang's trip, experiences, and insights are naturally accurate and rich, and can be used as research materials for us in every way. We have a new guide. This is the second reason for a warm welcome. Border issues should be studied with the attention of the Chinese people. Therefore, we hope that the government leaders who manage border affairs will provide us with practical materials at any time within the scope of possibility, so that the conclusions of the research will not contradict the actual situation of the border. Then, Mr. Huang stood up and gave a speech, roughly saying that border issues are indeed important issues for China today. He has always been interested in them. This trip to Tibet was mainly spent on the road, so the observation time was very short. In general, he felt that the people of Tibet were simple and sincere, with a strong inward feeling, which was very good. At the same time, he felt that there were three advantages in the relationship between China and Tibet that were gratifying: (1) Tibet and China have a long history of more than 2,000 years, and the past feelings were very good, so the inward feeling is strong. This is the first advantage. (2) The border policies of China's past dynasties have all adopted a policy of appeasement and provided practical assistance to the border people. The Tibetan people are very grateful for this kind of policy. This kind of lenient border policy is the second advantage. (3) China's national spirit has always upheld humanity, justice, and equality for all five ethnic groups in the country under the current Prime Minister, which is beyond the reach of foreign countries and makes the Tibetan people more determined to look inward. This great spirit of nation-building is the third advantage. Since China has these three advantages, it can move the border people, and the anesthesia and temptation of foreigners are not easy to implement. Although China has these three advantages, border issues cannot be considered resolved from now on. We should continue to restore, preserve, and promote this good historical nation-building spirit and border governance policy, and further achieve the ability to provide substantial assistance and protection, so that the border people will not feel foreign oppression and have other concerns. Then, the inward-looking heart can be permanently strengthened. If there are only the above three advantages without substantial assistance, it will still be difficult to solve today's border issues. However, the cultivation of this strength depends on the efforts of the compatriots across the country, and I especially hope that the gentlemen of the Northwest Problem Research Association will lead and promote it, and look forward to its success. This is an important matter that I felt this time. As for the geography, religion, politics, economy, society, customs, etc. of Tibet, there is no shortage of things to talk about, but due to time constraints, I can't say everything at once. I will contribute to you in detail later when I have the opportunity to serve as a reference for research. I hope everyone will work hard, and I am willing to follow behind and do my best. Next, the members successively raised various questions, and Mr. Huang answered them one by one, discussing each other. There were also many important reports and interesting lectures on the details of Nepal, India, Overseas Chinese in Southeast Asia, and the Philippines. The guests and hosts dispersed at 9:30 pm, all in good spirits.

The Delegation to the Philippines Will Depart Soon 116

Another Meeting Was Held Yesterday to Elect Important Officials

According to the Central News Agency, the Chinese Tourism Delegation to the Philippines held another meeting yesterday at 4:30 pm in the conference room on the third floor of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, based on the previous meeting, before departure. Over twenty people attended, including Wang Xiaolai, Pan Gongzhan, Chen Songyuan, Zhu Shaoping, Chen Xiaodie, Xu Xiaochu, and Wang Tianshen. The details of the meeting are recorded as follows:

Chairman's Report

Chairman Wang Xiaolai first stood up and reported that, as of now, applications have been submitted and approved for those who will board the President Jackson ship on the afternoon of the 19th and set sail for the Philippines on the morning of the 20th. They include Chen Songyuan and his wife, Pan Gongzhan and his wife, Wang Xiaolai and his wife, Chen Xiaodie and his wife, Xu Xiaochu and his wife, You Jusun, Wang Tianshen, Chen Xiangtao, Du Jinsheng, Zhu Shaoping, Zheng Fangzheng, Zheng Xuejun, Mao Heyuan, Le Fucheng, Zai Yizhong, Zhong Guoquan, Yao Xijiu, Chen Yonglin, Wang Yanqing, and Sun Lanting, totaling twenty-six people. In addition, the head of the delegation, Mr. Wang Rutang, has already gone to the Philippines in advance and will meet in Manila. Mr. Li Yingsheng has also gone to Hong Kong in advance and will board the ship in Hong Kong. The entire delegation totals twenty-eight people. Among them, Mr. Chen Songyuan and Mr. Mao Heyuan are representing the Ningbo Native Association in Shanghai and will also go to the Philippines to visit the Ningbo overseas Chinese in the Philippines. He then read out the telegrams from the Manila Chinese Chamber of Commerce and the Consul General stationed there, and said that the trip will board the ship on the evening of the 19th and leave the port on the morning of the 20th, and can take a short trip to Hong Kong. They will arrive in Manila on the 25th, which is just right to participate in the Carnival that has already opened on the 16th. On the 4th, which is the closing day of the Chinese Association, they can take the Asia Queen ship back to China on the same day and arrive in Shanghai on the 10th.

Election of Officials

In addition to the already elected Wang Rutang as the head of the delegation and Wang Xiaolai as the deputy head of the delegation, the following important officials were elected yesterday: Chief Secretary Chen Xiangtao, Chinese Secretary Pan Gongzhan, Assistant Chen Xiaodie, English Secretary Zhu Shaoping, Assistant Wang Tianshen, and Accountant Wang Tianshen.

Preparatory Procedures

Chief Secretary Chen Xiangtao then reported on the preparations for the trip, saying that ship tickets and luggage labels, etc., will be delivered to the members next Tuesday. Passport procedures have been entrusted to the China Travel Service. The wives also need two photos, but the signature can be signed by the husband as an agent. The exchange procedures have also been entrusted to Mr. Zhang Minliang of the Shanghai Bank to handle everything nearby. In addition to the ship tickets, each person needs at least three to five hundred yuan, which can be exchanged for Hong Kong dollars and Philippine pesos from the Shanghai Bank in batches for use after arriving at the port.

Resolutions

(1) Telegraph the Philippine Chinese Chamber of Commerce to report the departure date and the list of members; (2) Telegraph thanks to Consul General Deng, and due to time constraints, will not go to southern Philippine for inspection; (3) After arriving in Manila, stay at the Great East Hotel and telegraph to reserve locations for 30 people; (4) Before returning to China, a banquet will be held in the Philippines to thank all sectors once, invite 150 guests, and prepare 1,000 yuan.

China Merchants Steam Navigation Company and Jing-Wu Railway Jointly Operate Water-Land Intermodal Transport 118

Effective March 5th

The state-owned China Merchants Steam Navigation Company (CMSNC) has signed water-land intermodal transport agreements with various railways, which have been implemented in sequence. The commercial operation of the intermodal transport between CMSNC and the Jiangnan Railway Company's Jing-Wu (Nanjing-Wuhu) line, after Mr. Zhou Fengtu signed the intermodal transport regulations with the Jiangnan Company, has now taken a further step. The intermodal transport fee has been negotiated. The Jiangnan Railway Company specially dispatched Section Chief Zhou of the Traffic Section to Shanghai to negotiate and sign the implementation date of the intermodal transport with CMSNC. It was decided yesterday that the intermodal transport will be implemented simultaneously in Shanghai and Wuhu from March 5th. The details are described as follows:

Intermodal Transport Locations

The intermodal transport locations agreed upon by CMSNC and the Jiangnan Railway Company, belonging to the land transport of the railway side, are nine stations in Wuhu: Dongmen (East Gate), Kazikou, Zhusizhuang, Miaojiazhuang, Wanzhi, Xiaogan, Wangjia, Xuancheng, and Sunjiabu. In the future, if the railway tracks are extended, CMSNC will be notified at any time. The intermodal transport locations belonging to the waterway, carried by CMSNC ships, are eleven ports: Hankou, Jiujiang, Datong, Anqing, Zhenjiang, Yantai, Tianjin, Ningbo, Shantou, Guangdong, and Shanghai (Nanjing was also included before the Jing-Wu line was opened to traffic).

Implementation Date

The goods transported by the Jiangnan Railway Company are mostly agricultural products. Wuhu's rapeseed and miscellaneous grains are the largest commodities. Xuancheng's paper is famous throughout the country but has not yet been transported to various places. In the past, inland sailing ships were used, which were expensive and delayed. Japanese merchants who came to purchase goods faced difficulties and spent a lot of time and money. Now that the Jiangnan Railway has been built, the difficulties of the past have been eliminated. Not only is transportation fast, but also the handling of export financing is possible, which has great benefits for the economy and production. The success of this water-land intermodal transport can not only recover the leakage of foreign shipping competition, but also reduce transportation costs. It has been decided that the road and sea will be implemented simultaneously in Shanghai and Wuhu from March 5th.

Low Freight Rates

Zhou Fengtu, the director of intermodal transport at CMSNC, spent several months consulting and painstakingly negotiating intermodal transport fees with the Traffic Section of the Railway Bureau, taking into account the interests of the cargo owners and reducing freight rates. The freight rates for various goods have been set, roughly divided into two categories: whole car and separate load. The unit of a whole car is ten or sixteen tons. Detailed price lists are available in separate "tariffs," which can be requested from the intermodal transport section of the Railway Bureau and CMSNC, or from various stations and branch offices. The loading of freight cars is divided into six links, and the procedures are very cautious. The payment of intermodal transport fees has been agreed to be divided into two types: prepaid and payable upon arrival, both of which can be chosen at the customer's convenience.

Connecting the Capital

The Jing-Wu Railway has been completed from Wuhu Dongmen to Sunjiabu. The railway tracks facing Nanjing are also being connected to the capital. According to Section Chief Zhou of the Traffic Section, the small train in Nanjing City has been leased by the Jiangnan Railway for a period of twenty years. Currently, the Jing-Wu section is actively under construction to connect the railway tracks with the Nanjing small train line. However, because there are walls and houses blocking the junction, the company is in the process of buying, dismantling, and repaving the tracks. The capital can be reached outside Nanjing City in March, and the railway will be connected to the capital railway in May. After the completion of the Jing-Wu Railway, the transportation of Anhui goods will be even more convenient.

Recovering Shipping Rights

In the past, foreign merchants engaged in a large amount of cargo transportation within the Yangtze River line. Among them, the British and Japanese companies had an advantage in the transshipment to various ports in the South and North Seas. Now that the Jiangnan Railway and CMSNC are jointly operating intermodal transport, the shipment of Anhui goods to the South and North Seas will seize the business of foreign merchants and switch to domestic ships, which will greatly recover shipping rights. Foreign shipping companies in this port, upon hearing the news of the intermodal transport on February 5th, wanted to strike first and had already reduced the freight for Anhui goods to various ports in the South Seas by 20% in order to compete and try to save their business.
