The Earth Is Round 174

— Zhen

The weather is getting colder, and school has let out for a winter break of over twenty days. The northwest wind is howling, blowing in gusts on the bare branches of the trees.

Ping'er had to hide at home to escape the cold. It was quite boring at home, and he was thinking of doing some work. Just then, his older brother, Jian'er, came in from outside and said, "Your teacher from school just came over and told Dad, 'Ping'er isn't very good at natural science.' So Dad asked me to teach you."

Ping'er lowered his head, feeling ashamed. Jian'er said, "There's no need to be ashamed, as long as you work hard. If there's anything you don't understand, just ask me." Ping'er went to the bookshelf to get a natural science book he had read before and asked, "Brother! The teacher said the earth is elliptical, but I'm a bit confused."

"In ancient China, people always said, 'Heaven is round, and the earth is square.' People in ancient Western countries also believed this. But the great Greek philosopher Aristotle said, 'During a lunar eclipse, the earth's shadow is projected onto the moon. Its edge is curved, so we know the earth is round.' The Egyptian astronomer Ptolemy also said, 'Ships entering the port see the bridge first, then the hull. Ships leaving the port see the entire ship first, then gradually disappear.' Furthermore, adventurers like Columbus and Magellan discovered the New World. These are all ironclad proofs that the earth is round.

In the seventeenth and eighteenth centuries, the British scientist Newton used the method of centrifugal force to speculate that the earth was liquid in the past, and its equator must have expanded due to rotation, while the poles were flattened. That's how we know the earth is a flattened ellipse, not a perfectly round ball." Jian'er excitedly told his younger brother, and Ping'er memorized each sentence.

Snatching the Sheep 175

— Yan Biguang

Time flies so fast. In the blink of an eye, the winter vacation is over, and we have to concentrate on studying again. But overworking the mind can also harm the body. It is best to play a game after using your brain for a while to balance a body that hasn't exercised for a long time. Snatching the Sheep is the best game.

Snatching the Sheep requires ten children to organize (at least five or six children). Today, let's assume there are ten children. Nine children act as the sheep, arranged in order according to their height. The tallest is the head, and the next tallest holds onto the back of the head sheep's collar with both hands, tightly, without letting go. This is repeated down the line. The person who is snatching the sheep stands in front of the sheep head. The sheep head is like an old sheep, and the eight behind are like lambs. The person who is snatching the sheep comes to snatch the lambs. The old sheep must protect the lambs from being snatched away, while the lambs must closely follow the old sheep to escape.

When the sheep snatcher sees that everyone is ready, they shout the countdown, one, two, three, and start snatching. Within five minutes, see how many sheep they can snatch. The snatched sheep must step aside. At the end, the old sheep and the snatched sheep are punished by lining up and hopping on one foot for ten feet. This is to punish the old sheep for not protecting the sheep well and the lambs for not escaping effectively. It is really interesting!

Harmony 176

— Yi'an

Posture for Children Writing 177

How Do Humans Spend the Winter? 178

— He Gongchao

In ancient times, when winter came, humans had no other way to keep warm except to hide in caves, wear animal skins, and burn firewood to warm their bodies. (Image 1) As civilization advanced, the methods of keeping warm became more complete. In modern times, when winter comes, people install coal stoves, electric heaters, and hot water radiators in their houses to warm the air. (Image 2) There are several kinds of clothing materials such as animal skins, wool, cotton, and woolen yarn, all of which can maintain body temperature. (Image 3) The above describes how people living in temperate zones spend the winter. The winter lives of people living in the arctic zones are different: They stack snow bricks into a circular shape, getting smaller and smaller towards the top, and cover the top with a round piece of snow. The gaps between the bricks are filled with loose snow. In this way, they create a windproof house that can be used to survive the winter. Their clothes are made entirely of animal skins. Boots are also made of long-haired skin. (Image 4)

Children, are we always afraid of winter? What ways can we use to keep our bodies always warm? Carry hand warmers and foot warmers? That will make your hands and feet prone to chilblains. Rely on a coal stove? That coal gas is unhygienic. Install an electric heater or hot water radiator? The price is too high and not every family can afford it. Therefore, the best way is to exercise often. Sufficient exercise will make you sweat even in winter.

Exercise often, and don't be afraid of the wind. That's the way to be a child of the new era! (Image 5)

Snow 179

— Hengjiu Qianchuo

The Formation of Snow: Water vapor encounters cold temperatures in the sky and turns into rain. Before the rain reaches the ground, it encounters even colder temperatures and turns into "snow." Individual pieces of snow are called snow pellets, and clumps of snow are called snowflakes. Both are generally called "snow."

The Properties of Snow: Snow is white and light. Its shapes vary and are very beautiful, including hexagonal and multi-angled shapes. (Image 1) However, sometimes snowflakes merge with each other, or after reaching the ground, they lose their original shape due to the prevailing temperature.

Snow Games: There are many types of snow games, such as building snowmen, throwing snowballs, rolling snowballs, pushing sleds, and playing snowball fights. These are all games that we like. (Image 2)

The Advantages and Disadvantages of Snow: The benefits of snow: 1. Beautifying the scenery; 2. Killing pests and insect eggs, which helps crops. This is why farmers hope it will snow in winter. The disadvantages of snow: 1. Damaging the young buds of plants; 2. Excessive snow can collapse houses and hinder transportation.

Year-Round Snow: Our country is located in the North Temperate Zone, so there is no year-round snow cover. In the Arctic, the Eskimos live in areas with year-round snow cover. Even their houses are made of ice and snow! (Image 3)

Dangerous Coal Gas 180

— Ren Chaojun

Children! Don't you often read newspapers? Aren't many people poisoned by coal gas every winter? Why do they die? The main reason is that the stoves they use only have two openings, and they close the doors and windows tightly when they sleep. Because burning coal produces carbon gas, this is a very common piece of knowledge. Coal produces carbon gas, which combines with the oxygen in the existing air to form carbon dioxide. However, the amount of oxygen in the room is limited. Combined with the breathing of the sleeping person, the air in the room becomes carbon dioxide. However, the carbon gas continues to be produced, and there is no oxygen to combine with it. It can only convert the carbon dioxide in the room into carbon monoxide. People continue to breathe, inhaling toxic carbon monoxide. Carbon monoxide is toxic and has coagulation properties. It mixes into the blood and replaces the oxygen, turning into carboxyhemoglobin, and solidifies, preventing circulation, so people die. Although some people say that water can detoxify, it can only add more oxygen to the room, but it cannot detoxify permanently, so this is a misconception. As for the method of rescue, the simplest thing is to open another hole in the stove and use a chimney to lead the carbon gas from the stove to the outside.

Children, you should pay attention to coal poisoning and explain it to your neighbors and classmates so that they all know the horror of coal poisoning and this inaccurate misconception.

The Doll Wearing a Leather Coat 181

— Zhang Nancun

Hai'er saw that Uncle Hu's pug next door was wearing a cotton coat and said, "Uncle Hu loves his pug very much and is afraid it will get cold, so he specially made a cotton coat for it to wear. What I love is my doll. In weather like this, it's still naked. Are people worse off than dogs?" He found some scraps of leather and asked his mother to make a leather coat for the doll to wear, like the decorations of foreign children. His mother said, "Toy dolls have no sensation and don't need to wear leather coats. We have our own body temperature. In winter, we wear leather and cotton clothes to prevent our body heat from dissipating, so we feel warm. But toy dolls have no body temperature. They don't feel cold without clothes, and they don't feel warm with clothes, so there's no need to make them." Hai'er said, "I understand that after this explanation, but it seems that toys should be suitable for the season. Winter requires wearing clothes. Why is the doll especially naked? Then it can only be used as a summer toy, not a winter toy. It would be more interesting to wear a leather coat. Please make it for me." His mother said, "Do you know? Last year's drought was very severe, and many disaster victims in various places were starving and freezing, with no clothes to keep warm. Are you also moved?" Hai'er said, "Then, can I donate all the lucky money and New Year's money that the elders have given me these past few days to help the disaster victims?" The mother greatly praised him and agreed to his request, making the doll's leather coat into clothes to wear. Hai'er looked at the doll wearing the leather coat and sang:

"Doll, wearing a leather coat, wears a leather coat and smiles happily, disaster victims are cold and hungry and crying, I am willing to use some of my money to help you."

Little Jokes 182

— Xidan

Two Stupid People

The father exchanged a joint giveaway coupon for two bags of chocolate candies. The child was extremely happy and asked his father how many he had exchanged. The father said, "One bag in my hand and one bag in my pocket. How many bags do you see in total?" The child replied, "Three bags." The father angrily scolded, "You stupid person, how many are you and me?" The child replied, "Two stupid people."

Two Columbuses

In a small school classroom, many elementary school students were attending class. After the teacher called the roll, he pointed to a student and asked, "Chen Weihua, do you know where America is that was discussed in the last lesson? Can you find it on the map?" Soon, Chen Weihua pointed it out. The teacher then turned to Li Ming and asked, "Then who discovered America?" Li Ming replied very straightforwardly, "That's me, Chen Weihua!"

The Voyages of Sinbad the Sailor (6) 183

— Xin Qing

I now knew how people obtain those precious gemstones from this deep valley. I had heard such stories before, but I couldn't believe them until I saw it with my own eyes.

When eagles have young, people come to this place. They stand near the edge of the steep cliffs and throw down large chunks of meat. The gemstones on the ground stick to the meat, and when these birds of prey take the meat and fly to their nests on the top of the cliffs, people climb to the outside of the nests, scare the birds away, and take the gemstones.

Having witnessed this, I came up with a plan to help me escape this valley, as I knew for sure that I couldn't climb out on my own.

First, I put all the gemstones I could find and the remaining food into my bag. Then, using my headscarf, I tied a large piece of meat to my body, and lay face down on the ground, with the bag of gemstones pressing tightly against my belt. Soon, many eagles flew down to eat and feed their young. One eagle grabbed the piece of meat I was tied to and flew me to a nest on top of a high cliff. The people I had mentioned indeed scared all the birds away, and one person came to the nest where I was.

He was shocked when he saw me. He thought I was there to steal his gemstones because this nest was his. You see, everyone has a nest, and they often consider it their own.

I thought he was going to mistreat me, so I told him not to worry, that I wasn't there to steal his gemstones.

I said, "In truth, I have more gemstones than you all combined. Moreover, you rely on chance to get them, while I picked them up in the valley."

I took out the gemstones from my bag and showed them to him. Before long, a large group of people surrounded me, and I told them everything that had happened since the ship abandoned me. I also gave a very valuable gemstone to the person who found me first. I happily spent the whole night with them. Afterward, I went with them to their camp and lived with them for a few days.

The Prevalence of Cutting Losses on Yarn and Flower Yarn 186

The market is heading toward a fatigued state, continuing to decline.

However, intelligence revealed a sudden softening at the third closing bell, as a cotton company cut losses on over ten thousand bales. The market shifted dramatically. As a result, all months fell by one or two jiao. News spread in the afternoon of large-scale liquidations by bullish investors. With such a large volume of chips in the market, the situation deteriorated, threatening floating positions. Those closing out positions surged in like a tide. Simultaneously, spot yarn sales became sluggish, causing the market to soften further. All months fell by four, five, six, or nine jiao. Sales included 5,050 bales from Da Feng, 1,000 bales from Da Fu, 1,050 bales from Geng Feng, 3,950 bales from Shen Chang, 1,650 bales from Sen Kang, 2,800 bales from Chang Feng, 1,450 bales from Run Kang, 850 bales from Xin Cheng, and 900 bales from Jun Chang. With few sellers, the market rose gradually. Bullish investors closed out March positions, which were absorbed by the Liverpool group and shifted to distant months. Most of the day's trading involved calendar spreads, with little off-market activity. The textile industry's appetite was also better. Hethorn estimated this week's mill consumption at 239,000 bales, and Liverpool's stock at 324,000 bales. Currently, the underlying strength is considerable. There is no selling pressure from the South. Bullish liquidations and scattered selling were absorbed by some pricing and short-covering. Women's Corner

Thoughts on Celibacy 194

— Ying Shen

In principle, a single life is an unhealthy life, and the existence of celibacy is unreasonable. However, under the current circumstances, many people have no choice but to live a single life. If we only circle around in theory without delving into reality, the conclusions we draw often have to be questioned. Therefore, although Mr. Yi Qiong repeatedly elaborated on the discussion of "The Ideals and Realities of Celibacy" (Women's Voice, Volume 3, Issue 7), he ultimately separated the ideal from reality.

Many people have no choice but to live a single life, which is an undeniable fact. However, we can observe this fact from two perspectives.

Some people (the absolute majority of those living single lives) do not embrace any celibacy at all, nor do they not need to get married (in fact, the opposite is true). It's just that the environment does not allow them to marry. Even if the standard for an ideal partner is low, marriage is still impossible for them.

Some people, although not born to be celibate and have never said "I don't need to get married," in order to "strive for social causes," find that not only can they not obtain a "happy marriage" or a "satisfactory partner," but they cannot even maintain a decent life. They feel that they should put the interests and needs of their personal life after the interests and needs of their cause. When a burden of "suffering" is placed before them, they willingly take it up because marriage "can indeed hinder their efforts in social causes."

The former are forced to do so, entirely determined by circumstances. The latter, in addition to objective reasons, also involve subjective factors through their reason. The former are single people but not celibates. There is no need to tell them the unreasonableness of celibacy, its anti-physiological nature, and so on, because they know it as well as you do. The latter can be called celibates (because they do it consciously). The focus of the problem lies here. No matter how you condemn celibacy with a death sentence and exile, they still have to remain single.

Of course, there are also many freaks in the world who regard celibacy as a final belief and adhere to it. There are also people who embrace celibacy as a strategy of "retreating to advance," hoping to sell themselves at a good price. But these people are in the minority, or at least only a part. Only these people are worth launching a total attack on their minds.

However, Mr. Yi Qiong seems to be treating a strand of cow hair as a whole cow.

It is true that Mr. Yi Qiong has said that for those who strive for social causes and consciously practice celibacy, this cannot be used as a reasonable basis for celibacy. He said that it "belongs to a social problem of a different nature." But here, Mr. Yi Qiong inevitably fixed the concept of "celibacy" as if celibacy is always unacceptable everywhere. I feel that this view is like regarding capitalism as absolutely lacking revolutionary nature, forgetting the specific, temporal, and spatial conditions. According to my immature understanding, we should generally adopt a negative attitude towards celibacy, but we must also have a little reservation. Erasing this reservation is no small mistake. Even for those who embrace celibacy to accomplish more important social causes, we should not only forgive them but also admire them. Among those people, advocating celibacy (which has been given a new content) and creating a trend of celibacy is definitely not a mistake.

In a word, regarding celibacy as an end is a ridiculously absurd act, but regarding it as a means is sometimes necessary. At the same time, those who practice celibacy as a means are actually fundamentally burying this "unreasonable" phenomenon, just as some people's death is for the sake of others' life.

I dare say that celibacy in this sense is definitely not "non-resistance." If a suitable metaphor is to be found in strategy, it can probably be said to be a "scorched earth" policy.

Immature opinions, please enlighten me, Mr. Yi Qiong.

Lectures on Women's Issues 195

— Jun Hui

Lecture 1: The Significance of Studying Women's Issues

Section 1: The Concept of Women's Issues

Simply put, the so-called women's issue is the issue of how to liberate women from their subordinate relationship to men. In other words, it is the issue of how to enable women to obtain a completely equal status with men in politics, economics, and society. It includes women's participation in politics, legal issues, educational issues, occupational issues, labor issues, and maternity protection issues, etc.

The reason why the women's issue has become an issue naturally has its historical reasons.

Historically, since the collapse of the primitive clan commune system and the emergence of private ownership of property, although inequality phenomena such as wealth, nobility, masters, and slaves have been found in human society, at the same time, women, who account for half of humanity, have also lost their status as "human beings" and become a kind of slave arbitrarily controlled by men. This phenomenon is particularly evident in feudal society. In the feudal era, the subordinate relationship of women to men was like the relationship of serfs to lords. It was no longer a relationship between people but a relationship between a person and an object. That is to say, men treated women like a cow or a chair, able to use them at will, abandon them at will, and even destroy them at will! In the "civilized" capitalist society, the subordinate relationship between men and women seems to have eased somewhat on the surface under the guise of so-called freedom and equality, but in fact, women still become objects of male oppression, playthings, and insults. In this way, the so-called women's issue has existed since the collapse of the clan commune system. In other words, this problem has existed with the continuation of a certain social system, rather than occurring by chance. However, it was promoted by the modern bourgeoisie only during the rise of capitalism.

When the commoner class built modern industrial cities on the ruins of feudal society and confronted and fought against feudal forces, they did propose many noteworthy issues, such as the issue of democracy in politics, the issue of equality in educational rights, the issue of freedom of occupation, the issue of serf liberation, and even the issue of women's liberation. However, the proposal of these issues was also for the sake of its own growth and development. Because the capitalist mode of production itself requires the solution of these problems.

However, the issue of women's liberation that the bourgeoisie wanted to propose and solve, like its political democratic issues, could not be thoroughly resolved. For example, women's participation in politics, educational issues, occupational issues, etc., have still not been fundamentally resolved in the most advanced European and American capitalist countries, and there is still a vast difference between the social status of men and women. The reason is very simple. That is because although the bourgeoisie overthrew the unreasonable feudal society, it also created an unreasonable social system itself. In this way, in an unreasonable society, fair and reasonable things will never exist.

When capitalism reached the stage of imperialism, essential changes were brought about in the issue of women's liberation. Especially after the European War, the number of female workers in various capitalist countries increased day by day, and they showed great strength in the labor movement. As a result, class divisions occurred in the past women's movement, resulting in the so-called liberation movement of working women, which was opposed to the equality of rights movement of middle-class intellectual women. On the other hand, the establishment of socialist countries in the Soviet Union and some other countries established a new society of true equality between men and women, fundamentally solving the women's issue that capitalist countries could not solve, giving women all over the world a very profound excitement and stimulation. As a result, the significance of the women's issue expanded from the issue of the liberation of women from men to the issue of the liberation of women from the social system.

Many reformist women's activists now believe that women can obtain a completely equal social status with men in the existing state, but this is just a dream. Naturally, in the current society, a small number of upper-class women have the possibility of receiving higher education, engaging in high-level occupations, or even participating in high-level political organizations, but this has nothing to do with the liberation of the entire women.

We believe that to solve the women's issue, the first is to eliminate women's social dependence on men, and the second is to eliminate women's economic dependence on men. However, the elimination of these two relationships cannot be realized under a male-centered social system. Therefore, the women's liberation movement will inevitably merge into the movement to change the unreasonable society and build an equal and reasonable society. Because only in this way can the fundamental liberation of women be achieved!

Combing Up 196

— Cao Ming

"Combing up" was once a very popular behavior in a certain period in Shunde County, Guangdong. When the silk industry was booming, it was excessively revered and regarded as sacred in places where mulberry silkworms were raised, and it was used by the girls there to resist unsatisfactory "marriages" in a hostile manner.

In the autumn of 1916, in Dunmu Township, Ah Xiu, the eldest daughter of Wu Furu, who owned several acres of mulberry fields, held her combing ceremony with the help of her capable aunt, without allowing anyone to stop her. Furu, a kind and amiable father, was very lively in greeting his daughter's companions, except for being dissatisfied with his sister, Ah Lan, buying an extra goose.

"What? A woman only has such a day once in her life, so let Ah Xiu have a decent one," Ah Lan replied to her brother, her mouth and the flesh of her cheekbones being pulled up by a knife scar on her left cheek, forming an ugly dimple. This woman, who didn't like to talk much except to explain things in a lecturing tone, was like a water chestnut that had been thrown into a salt jar, often making people forget her existence. Even after dinner that night (because those married female guests left after eating, rarely playing with the girls who had already combed up or were yet to be married until dawn), when the remaining girls surrounded Ah Xiu like a besieged city, snatching olives, the crooked-mouthed aunt stood in a corner of the room, as if supervising the battle with her hands, without smiling or saying anything. In short, no matter what the occasion, it was very rare for her to express any emotion. As if seduced by those intense emotional gestures, she reluctantly agreed to the girls' request and told a story with a didactic meaning that was very suitable for her status.

Like a group of mischievous little sparrows, the young women deliberately indulged themselves in this night. They did whatever came to their mouths or hands. The furniture and beds in the room were all moved from their original positions. Several mischievous fellows enthusiastically played various roles, performing a temporarily composed play to insult the groom. Ah Xiu, who had just had her hair combed into a bun by a long-lived elder, was teased and humiliated with honorable shyness by completely well-meaning vulgar words, making her companions even happier.

"Crooked-mouth Aunt Lan, tell us something, huh? Didn't you join the Sisterhood?" a girl with a pointed chin of eighteen or nineteen years old suddenly shouted towards the corner. Knowing that people agreed with her proposal, she continued even more excitedly, "Tell us how your mouth got crooked, was it your own fault or..."

"Based on what you think, can my mouth tell any nice stories?" Aunt Lan smiled, her mouth even more crooked like a sweet star fruit. "How about I sing a song for you?"

The girls shook her body frantically, and she closed her eyes, raised her head, and sang the melancholic words in a very heavy, slow tone, like the dying cry of a wild beast crushed by a large stone.

"Using thread and needle:

For the sake of, a free body!

Good sisters, don't complain about tight clothes. You say,

Rather let the flower wither than let the butterfly invade!"

She opened her eyes wide, looked at everyone, and then gave a strange laugh. "You eat too little rice, you wouldn't know. Was the Sisterhood like your muddle-headed appearance now? Alas, this is a sacred matter! Which woman, when unwilling to die and meet the Jade Emperor, doesn't try to be as clean as Guanyin? So those who joined the party had to swear never to approach men. If they were forced by their parents to marry, then, before getting into the sedan chair, the sisters would have to sew up her little shirt and pants skillfully and carefully, and everyone would cry and sing as if their mother had died." She spoke very clearly, as if wanting people to put every word into their ears. "But once, there was a joke in Shibu Township. That girl was a distant cousin of my mother, who grew up relying on a pair of fierce elder brothers and sisters-in-law. She got married, and her underwear was sewn up by the sisters. Things were very coincidental—her man was a very clever fellow; on the wedding night, he carried a pair of scissors on his body, preparing to cut open those stitches; but unfortunately, my mother's cousin was not a piece of wood. In the rush, she pierced her belly—"

"Ah, is she going to die?" someone shouted.

Many girls worriedly grimaced and huddled behind Ah Xiu, who was sitting like the Buddha, as if playing a game of stacking Arhats.

"The matter was very simple: she fell out with her in-laws and turned against her elder brothers and sisters-in-law, but she lived a relaxed life, respected like a hero. Until the early summer of her twenty-fourth year—a very dull noon—she and the single out-of-town fireman in the silk factory, like two silkworms that hadn't spun silk, were seen behind the silk factory's warehouse, under the grass shed where no one usually went..."

"Oh, why was that? ——"

"It's like this, too bad!" a girl said mechanically.

"Who knows what this is for!" The crooked-mouthed woman closed her eyes again. "She actually did that. Such dishonorable things happen often! But think about it, are our ears willing to load these poisonous juices?"

Everyone was very neatly silent for a very short time, and then expressed their opinions unsystematically. They felt great interest in this kind of question, just like they needed some encouragement and stimulation in that gloomy and monotonous life...

"Do you understand, children? Have you really not heard this story?"

"Is there more? Tell us a little more!" a young and fat girl said, her voice a little unnatural, like a machine pretending to be calm after a big thunder.

Overseas Women's News

World Women's Congress 197

— Min Jun

Recently, progressive women from various countries, in view of the inherent contradictions and various problems that cannot be solved in various countries, are now fraught with crises, fearing that this will lead to a world war; at the same time, since Western fascism gained power in Europe, it has spared no effort to oppress the women's movement. For example, the status of women in German society today has been almost completely deprived, and the slogan "Women, go back to the kitchen" is sung loudly. Therefore, a World Women's Congress was launched, which was held from August 4th to 7th last year in the Mutual Aid Society Hall (Ｐalaio　de　la　Mntnahte) on Mengci Street (Ｒue　Monge) in the 5th arrondissement of Paris. This journal has briefly recorded the news. The details of the meeting are listed again as follows:

There are many matters discussed at this conference. The women representatives of various countries have different ideals and beliefs, so the debates when discussing the proposals are often extremely fierce, but they are completely unanimous on the important points. They understand that in today's capitalist society, so-called women's liberation and world peace are impossible: they all acknowledge that (the bad environment of capitalism creates economic panic, economic panic promotes outward-aggression imperialism, and when imperialism reaches maturity, it intensifies war, which is an inevitable result. At the same time, capitalism is the enemy of the liberation of ordinary women and working women.)

They recognized the root of these obstacles to the healthy development of society. Therefore, the representatives unanimously voted on the resolutions proposed by the various committees. Based on those resolutions, it can be seen that this women's congress is of great significance, and women's thoughts are profound and their vision is broad. There are many resolutions and cannot be listed one by one: all the representatives hold a spirit of firm struggle. The opinions of the conference can be summarized into two factions:

The Young Women's Faction advocates: "Women all over the world should quickly seek the early realization of the women's anti-war and anti-imperialism declaration;

The Pacifist Faction advocates: "Women all over the world should refuse to participate in all work that engages in aggressive war or prolongs hostility."

Therefore, it was decided that women should not work in imperialist arsenals that manufacture killing tools; women all over the world should not participate in aggressive military organizations. The Lyon branch of the French Women's Peace and Freedom League (Ｌa　section　de　la　Ligne　des　femmes　pour　la　paix　et　Lyon　de　la　liberte) proposed that women all over the world should not participate in any aggressive military rescue teams. Later, female railway workers and the wives of railway workers put forward a noteworthy proposal: when imperialism engages in aggressive war, they should try their best to stop it. They cooperate with railway workers, shipbuilding workers, sailors, metallurgical workers, and road transport workers, and the means they take are as follows:

A. Oppose the manufacture and transportation of military supplies;

B. Stop the transportation of all military and police forces that suppress workers struggling for survival.

Female teachers teach that they must refuse imperialist aggressive propaganda when teaching.

In addition to the resolutions, the conference also issued a declaration, and a few sentences are specially excerpted below:

"We women see that mankind is threatened by unprecedented disasters. We have the right to resist and overthrow this disaster, this is our duty and mission..."

The conference also listed the resolutions into a code, summarizing that they demand absolute liberation of women, equal status in society, and opposition to imperialism and war: in addition, they engage in the liberation movement of oppressed people—without distinction of race or nationality. They believe that since women are human beings, they should be allowed to develop freely, their abilities, and allowed to work freely.

They have now returned to engage in the work of their transformation plan. It is still unknown what the effect will be in the future, but this conference has aroused great attention from world opinion.

Note to those who submit letters to the Legal Advisory Column

(1) Must specify the Women's Garden Legal Advisory Column

(2) The narrative must be concise and clear, not scribbled, not written horizontally, and not in pencil

(3) The letter must contain the real name and address. Those who wish to use a pseudonym when publishing can declare in advance

(4) Regarding the issue of women's inheritance, the date of death of the deceased must be stated

Introducing "The Life of Soviet Women" 198

— Zi Wen

Written by Fan, published by Shanghai Wenku of Shen Bao, actual price of two dimes

The new country of the "Soviet Union," although it has long been recognized by various countries in the world, and China and the Soviet Union have resumed diplomatic relations for many years, most people still talk about the Soviet Union with horror. The Soviet women in most people's minds are still occupied by concepts such as "common wives" and "state-owned." But in fact, what is the life of Soviet women like? Talking about this "Life of Soviet Women" can give you a clear answer.

According to the author's preface, he has studied in the Soviet Union for many years and visited many centers of large-scale industrialization and agricultural collectivization. Therefore, he has a real understanding and experience of the life of Soviet women.

What is here is a description of real life, without exaggeration or propaganda. It is not a legendary myth. Anyone who has doubts about the life of Soviet women must read it.

The whole book consists of sixteen chapters, including family life, marriage and divorce, love, children, increased cultural level, economic liberation, women's labor and pure rights protection, political life, decoration, music, and women's publications, totaling more than 30,000 words.

Mr. Pu Shunqing, Guan Lu, Guo Zhenyi, Xie Qing, Qian Yuzhen, She Ying, and others:

Please send a replacement imprint for remittance.

However, yesterday I heard a news item in your newspaper about the remarriage of a phoenix. Not only was there no criticism from society, but the new words of affection were broadcast as beautiful words. This person believes that this person and Mr. Xiong are both living in the same world, the only difference is the gender. Amateur Chat

Professional Women and Reading 199

— Wu

For the sake of life, I have been pressed in the vise of a profession for ten years. In the past ten years, I have wasted my time and made no progress; at the same time, I have met many others with the same problem who have made little or no progress, and my heart is saddened when I think about it.

In modern times, lower-middle-income jobs generally involve more than eight hours of work a day. After work, men and women naturally rarely come into contact with books after returning home exhausted, but it seems even more so for women. Therefore, it is very difficult to ask women for some common sense, whether they are in the family or in social service. This situation is mostly due to the environment, and partly due to one's own failure to break the inherited habits.

Inherited habits: women have long been isolated from knowledge and society, and have no interest in books. Although times have changed and women often go to school, the biggest purpose of reading is to get a diploma; the biggest use of a diploma is, first, to find a job, and second, to use it as decoration. When a woman gets a diploma and finds a job, she has reached the final stage of reading and has fulfilled the greatest role of reading; afterwards, she lives a plain and unpursued life, just like a woman who has not read.

As for the environment, women are still in women's environment today. Married professional women are troubled by housework after returning from work. Unmarried professional women mostly associate with aunts and sisters, and mostly talk about decorations, entertainment, love, and gossip. Because the national situation is becoming more and more dangerous and the pressure is increasing, men's heads are lowered by three feet, and women are not allowed to raise their heads even more. Not only is there no opportunity to enlighten her with meaningful and soaring ambitions, but there is only opportunity to suppress her with dust, so she becomes meaningless without knowing it.

However, time is the true pearl of life, and knowledge is the true grain of life. It is helpless for professional women to use part of the pearls as firewood and part of the grain as dregs due to the limitations of life: if they simply abandon both completely, making their lives exhausted, withered, and dim, not only will they not be able to contribute much to society, but society will not need you either; as a result, the profession that you rely on will also become a problem. Therefore, for the sake of enriching life and maintaining a profession, professional women must find ways to read and seek some new knowledge. The most important things here are:

1. Read newspapers and magazines: Newspapers and magazines—especially newspapers—are full of social phenomena and world phenomena; on them, you can understand the international situation, the situation in China, and your own position. Then study how to deal with the situation and devote yourself to meaningful work.

2. Read books within the industry: If the profession is sometimes not entirely consistent with what you have learned, it will be easy to be incompetent, so you need to study more. Sometimes what you have learned may even be consistent with the profession, but you must always study new theories and new methods, so that your knowledge and skills will improve day by day and not be pushed back by the new waves;

3. Read books on social sciences: Professional women have entered society, and if they still only value the family and do not strive to understand society, they are wasting their lives. Why is one's own profession so shaky? Why is the social situation so unstable? Tracing back layer by layer, exploring the source, books on social science will be able to give you answers.

In short, today, professional women rarely see any writing in their eyes except for fashion magazines, movies, or advertisements for discounted foreign goods. As a result, the knowledge that she slightly instilled in her early years has evaporated and dried up after many years. Some women who have been in office for a long time often become stubborn and shallow, and are unbearable to talk to those with a little common sense. This has become a common and painful phenomenon. Professions solve life, and solving life extinguishes spirituality; and some people are complacent and content with this, so how can women grow

Great Shanghai Scenery

A Visit to the Laborers' Nursery 200

— Shen Qianli

I had this thought for a long time—to visit a laborers' nursery. In the end, every time the thought stirred, I was entangled by other things.

This day, I made a special resolution—I had to go and see it. So, at four o'clock in the afternoon, I found the nursery I had been longing to visit on Penglai Road.

The nursery was located in a five-room building in the Qinpanfang alley. Upon entering, there was a living room that also served as an auditorium. In the center, a portrait of the Party, the Nation, and Dr. Sun Yat-sen was solemnly hung. Below it, there was a large dining table and four sofas, all covered with snow-white cloth covers. As soon as I stepped over the threshold, I instinctively felt a solemn and lonely atmosphere rushing towards me, and I was stunned for a moment. After a while, a tea servant came out from inside, and I handed him my business card to take in. When the tea servant came out again, a lady followed behind, wearing a blue cotton qipao, with glasses and a smile on her face, walking towards me, asking, "Is this Mr. Shen?" What can I do for you? Her attitude was noticeably very kind.

I quickly stood up, smiling and answering, "I wouldn't dare! I heard that your institution is doing very well, so I made a special trip here to visit. Yes, I haven't had the pleasure of asking your name yet?"

"My name is Zhu; there's not much achievement to speak of, we've only just started." She gestured for me to sit down and then sat down again.

"You're too kind, the achievements must be very good, I believe it. But I don't know how the organization here is structured. I hope that if Ms. Zhu is not busy, you can tell me." I began to present my request to her.

"Sure, I don't have anything to do right now; but our organization is very simple, I'm afraid there aren't any good materials to provide to Mr. Shen." She smiled faintly, and then said, "The director here is Mr. Li Ting'an, and there is also a vice-director, followed by an administrative and nanny director, as well as a teacher and three nanny trainees."

"The nanny director is Ms. Zhu, right?" I asked tentatively.

"..." She smiled slightly.

"What is the monthly income and expenditure here?"

"The recurring expenses are four hundred and fifty dollars. The building is provided free of charge by the Education Bureau, so with so much funding, the expenses are sufficient. However, the fees for childcare are pitifully low, with only thirteen children in total, generating only twenty dollars of income per month. This amount of money is not enough to cover the living expenses of two children!" She couldn't help but laugh as she said this.

"The children entrusted here are mostly from the working class, right?"

"Well! It's not as much as people generally assume. Among the thirteen children, five are from the working class, one from the education sector, three from the business sector, three from the police and national defense sector, and one from the banking sector—"

"Banking sector?" I interrupted her and asked.

"Yes!" She said calmly, "This child's father is a staff member of the Zhonghui Bank. Because he has five children, this is the youngest one. The mother really can't take care of all five children so thoroughly, so he came here to

Page 22

ask us to entrust this child here. Of course! The nursery is supposed to serve the general public, so we agreed to his request. However, when the number of working-class children here exceeds the quota in the future, we will still have to notify him to take the child back." She explained in detail.

It felt like a stone had been lifted from my heart, and I felt lighter. I then asked, "What are the hours for childcare and how do you educate them?"

"Mr. Li believes that, in terms of the child's feelings for the family, they should not be separated from their families. Daytime care is due to family circumstances, which is not a problem, but they must go back at night. Moreover, boarding at the nursery would place too much responsibility on us. So, the childcare hours here are from 7:00 to 8:00 in the morning, when family members bring the children to the nursery; and from 6:00 to 7:00 in the afternoon, when family members pick them up again. Each child's family member is issued a 'care certificate,' which they must bring when picking up the child; otherwise, the nursery staff will send the child home. We don't accept boarding children for now. The children eat five meals a day: breakfast at 7:30 in the morning, a snack at 10:00, lunch at 12:00. Nap time is from 12:30 to 2:30 in the afternoon, every day. Some children haven't developed this habit at home, so when they first come here, they can't sleep as quietly as the other children, but after a few days, they gradually get used to it. There is another snack at 3:30 in the afternoon, and dinner at 6:00. Each meal consists of a soup and two dishes, and each person has a small basin and two small bowls, eating separately like a Western meal."

"Are the children's clothes also provided by the nursery?"

"Yes, we even made a special uniform: the shirt is white and the pants are blue, and the style is not bad. However, the families of the children all have this idea, thinking that wearing the nursery's clothes doesn't seem very elegant. So now we don't give them clothes to wear." She said, standing up and inviting me, "Mr. Shen, if you want to visit, I can accompany you upstairs now."

"Okay, okay; please lead the way!" I hurriedly agreed.

Passing through the living room, we reached the office area. There were three desks and some calligraphy and paintings hanging on the walls, arranged in an orderly manner. Behind this room, there was also a clothing room, filled with more than a dozen wardrobes taller than people, full of children's clothes. When children arrive at the nursery in the morning, they must first come here to change into the nursery's uniform; and in the evening, they change back into their own clothes before going home. Going further in from here, we reached the washroom, which had three flushing "shower heads," twelve washbasins, towels, toothbrushes, and mouthwash cups. The washing area was a mound made of cement, perfectly suited to the height of the children when they leaned on it to wash their faces. The children washed their faces themselves, with the nannies only standing by to supervise.

"The children's washing and bathing are assisted by nannies, right?" I asked her.

"Of course. Even when washing their faces, some children still don't wash them clean. But I hope to cultivate a sense of independence in them. Bathing was originally scheduled once a day, but later some of the children's families requested that it be extended a bit in this cold weather, changing it to once every three days. Look, isn't there a large stove over there?" She pointed to a stove over there and looked at me.

After visiting the bathroom for a while, we turned to the children's nap room upstairs. This room was formed by connecting three front rooms, and outside was the Municipal Zoo. From the glass window on this side, we could see many exotic animals in the zoo. The air in the room was as fresh and abundant as in a park. There were thirty small iron beds neatly arranged here, with a quilt and a pillow on each bed, covered with snow-white sheets, arranged as cleanly as a ward in a top-notch hospital. Next to the bedroom was the playroom, which occupied two rooms on the floor. The room had children's swings, seesaws, rocking horses, and bicycles, displayed like a toy store. In addition, there were three cages of canaries chirping, making every child look at them and smile. At the east end of the playroom, there were twenty-four tables and chairs, neatly arranged in two rows, like a small-scale meeting place. When the children got tired of playing, they would sit here to rest, and some children were still talking here. They suddenly saw me, a stranger, walk in, and they all stopped talking at the same time, revealing a pair of round, small eyes looking at me.

"How old are the oldest of these children?" I turned and asked her.

"Four years old! Those sitting here are only a little over two years old." She pointed to the children and said.

The children's eyes flickered and looked at each other again, as if they already knew that we were talking about them.

Walking down from the playroom was the dining room. Here were the same twenty chairs as upstairs. On the other side, there were also two large tables, and the bowls and many eating utensils were all neatly arranged in two large cabinets as tall as the floorboards. During meal times, the staff and children ate at the same time; however, the children had snacks in the morning and evening, but the staff did not. Next to the dining room, there was also a clinic and an isolation room. If the children had common minor ailments, they could go to the clinic for treatment. There were as many Western medicines as in a hospital, as well as an operating bed and a scale. The children's bodies were examined twice a month, and their weight was checked once a week. If a child with an infectious disease was found, they would be sent to the isolation room for a doctor to diagnose, and the family members would be notified to take the child back. The nursery could also introduce reliable doctors to treat them.

The doctor hired by the nursery was German, and he came to the nursery twice a week, but if a child suddenly fell ill, he could be notified to come on a temporary basis.

I had seen all the equipment and conditions. At that time, I only had one feeling, and I also said to Ms. Zhu, who had warmly welcomed me for the visit:

"It is indeed a pity that nurseries like this are not yet widely established in China!"

Vocational Guidance

Marriage - A Profession for Women 202

— Yongnian

In Shanghai, whether you're renting a house or meeting a new friend, people either ask, "Where are you getting rich?" or "What business does your husband do?" These are both ways of asking what your profession is. To describe professional activity as "getting rich" or "doing business" is consistent with the meaning of professional activity in today's society. Because in today's society, those who engage in professional activity are merely doing so for their personal lives. So, the question "What business do you do?" naturally expresses the nature of profession in today's society, and the question "Where are you getting rich?" also indicates where you are making money to support your life, highlighting the fundamental characteristics of profession in today's society. Thus, we can generally say that profession refers to the means and methods by which individuals maintain their lives.

Under this definition of profession, we can say that there are no unemployed people in society. Because being an official, soldier, businessman, teacher, selling articles, working in a factory, or farming in the countryside are certainly professions, but selling herbal medicine on the street, performing tricks, telling fortunes, and even being prostitutes or beggars also fit the definition of using specific means and methods to sustain one's personal life. Doesn't this mean everyone is employed and everyone has a profession?

We won't discuss other matters, but now, based on this definition of profession, let's talk about how marriage is also a profession for women in today's society.

Since the Industrial Revolution, many women have been liberated from their families and allowed to find work in society, which is called women having occupational freedom. Indeed, in the past, women could not work in industrial institutions, government agencies, or any public institutions, but what about women today? They can be factory workers, shop assistants, teachers, nurses, lawyers, and they can also be clerks, committee members, and even ambassadors, consuls, ministers, etc., in public institutions. If we expand the scope according to the definition of profession mentioned above, then prostitutes who openly display their signs and are protected by law are also professionals. We should not exclude them from the number of professionals because they are lowly. We must know that they are forced to adopt the method of "getting rich" or "doing business" to maintain their lives!

In China, although women now have considerable opportunities to participate in social professional activities, most are still confined at home without finding a way out, so the opportunities for them to freely choose a profession are still very few. Although rural women can participate in agricultural production activities nearby, they generally do not have an independent economic status and therefore live as subordinates to others. Especially unmarried women, who are simply raised in the families of their parents and brothers, and cannot even talk about independently exchanging the right to live by any means or method. For this reason, most adult unmarried women in China mostly take marriage to men as wives as the only way out, using this as a means and method to maintain their lives. In this way, we can say that marriage is the profession of most women. This is by no means a harsh word; in fact, this is the mentality of most women, and even the social mentality. Old-fashioned unmarried women certainly regard marriage as a lifelong problem to be solved. Once married to a husband, they rely on their husband for life to solve their livelihood problems. Even many modern young women, even if they are intellectuals, have the same mentality. When they reach a certain age, they focus on finding a lover and getting married. Although the solution to the marriage problem is also included, they mostly no longer strive to deepen their own knowledge and talents, always believing that getting married is a final destination. Therefore, among them, they either choose lovers and pay special attention to whether they have property, ability, and profession to maintain her life and ensure the permanent security of her life, or directly hope that getting married can immediately solve the livelihood problem. What is this if not the mentality of taking marriage as a profession? The social psychology is also the same, and everyone believes that women's marriage is the key to solving her problem. A few days ago, I saw a women's magazine that said that women's economy originally included men's economy, so even if women cannot find a profession in society, livelihood problems and even social problems will not occur, because there is no professional problem on them. Doesn't this argument clearly say that women's marrying people as wives is their profession, and the purpose of managing their lives has been achieved?

We are not saying that women should take marriage as a profession and should be satisfied with it, but rather that when women's economy cannot be independent and social professions are not fully open to women in the present society, they and the society will inevitably form the mentality of taking marriage as a profession, becoming their unavoidable hardship.

Marriage Guidance

Love and Age 203

— Shao Wen

I am not a believer in love above all else. I don't think that love is the primary meaning of life. On the contrary, it is subordinate to the highest meaning of life. However, when it comes to talking about love, I think that there must be great love only under genuine love. Love should not be constrained by any traditional ideas. As long as a man and a woman truly love each other, they can unite without asking for the approval of God or irrelevant people.

But what does age have to do with love? I think the emotion of love is not created out of thin air but is produced under certain existing practical conditions. A truly loving couple, their living interests and their thoughts must not have major contradictions, and their ages must be roughly equal; otherwise, genuine love in them will have nowhere to arise. I dare say that a girl who believes in anarchism will never truly love a timid miser; a young man who is unwilling to degenerate and determined to strive for his future in a hard life will never accompany a modern girl full of snobbish vanity and holding hedonism every day; similarly, it is difficult for me to believe that a young girl will really love a gray-haired old man. I have never believed in the matter of "pure spiritual love" in my life. That is the prejudice of ascetics. I believe that love must be a unity of spirit and flesh. If I am not mistaken, then please think about it, how can a unity of spirit and flesh love happen between a young girl and a gray-haired old man? If it really happens, that is indeed a big strange thing!

Of course, I am not saying that only men and women who are nineteen and a half years old will fall in love. No, what I mean is that only men and women of similar age are more likely to have genuine love. The so-called similarity means not to believe that it is too far away. If a young girl marries an old man of the same age as a planting expert, that is a bitter thing because the age is too dissimilar.

At this point, even if we take a step back and admit that young ladies can fall in love with "vigorous" old men, it must be because she really loves him, loves his knowledge and talent, and thus loves everything about him, that is correct. Otherwise, this love cannot be considered great love but is produced under some base consciousness. To be more specific, if she really loves him when she is held in the arms of her old lover, that is of course very good; on the contrary, if she is thinking about foreign money and what position at that time, and smiling in her heart, quickly thinking about the young and strong car driver or her old lover's young son, and therefore feels joy and pain at the same time in the middle, then it cannot be pleasing!

However, in fact, it is said that the god of love, Venus, has long been the concubine of the god of wealth, Marshal Zhao Gongming, and human love has been dominated and managed by the axe of the god of wealth. Therefore, most of the loves with incompatible ages are forcibly formed under the magic of foreign money and banknotes. The marriages of girls with parents and elders and old men are mostly caused by parents who love other people's money; the loves of "free" young ladies without parents and elders and old and decaying people are mostly produced under the direct drive of money by the parties.

Life

Pierhead Cart 204

— Han Ying

The so-called "pierhead cart" means pushing a cart to catch up with the pier. Needless to say, the people pushing this kind of cart are farmers, but there are also those who do this as a profession.

Due to the economic decline of rural areas in recent years, the phenomenon of farmers leaving their villages has become increasingly widespread. Some, amidst severe disasters and famines, dress up as refugees and go out to seek food. Others go to the cities to sell their labor at low prices to make a living. In addition, there are some more conservative farmers who, although they still work in the countryside, often find that their harvests are not enough to sustain their families. They are forced to find some side jobs to do in addition to their main occupation.

Pushing a "pierhead cart" is necessary for these farmers as a kind of side job. This kind of work is mostly short-term and temporary, and mostly done during the slack farming season, so it does not hinder farming much. The cities and towns they go to are mostly no more than two hundred li away, usually only a hundred li or so, so they are never more than a day or two's journey from home. Due to this convenience, it is no wonder that farmers rush to do this kind of work, fearing that they will be late.

However, pushing this kind of cart is not an easy task. This cart is a kind of single-wheeled cart that we often see. There is a "trick" to pushing this kind of cart, and you must understand this "trick" in order to move it happily and effortlessly. Sometimes, just using brute force will not work. Therefore, this kind of work cannot be done by farmers who are "not in the know." In an ordinary rural village, even if there are a hundred strong men, there may not be more than ten skilled pierhead cart pushers. There are many farmers who would like to earn some money by pushing pierhead carts, but their abilities limit them. If it were not for this reason, there might be even more people pushing pierhead carts.

In Anqing—what has been said above mostly refers to the situation in Anqing and nearby areas, although this situation is not unique to this area—every year during "late winter" is the most active time for pierhead cart drivers. In the eleventh month of the lunar calendar, farming is generally finished, and farmers can use their surplus labor to exchange for money in the towns and cities. They can travel in groups of three or five to the city of Anqing. They bring their own empty carts, planning to return fully loaded. When they arrive in Anqing, the cart transportation agencies in Anqing will accept them. They can wait in these agencies for their good fortune to arrive.

In Anqing, there are many such cart transportation agencies. Just on "He Street" outside the West Gate, there are more than ten. Farmers from western counties mostly "stay" in the cart transportation agencies outside the West Gate, and most of their business is to go to western counties. The situation in the north and east of the city can be inferred from this, so there is no need to mention it here.

The treatment of these customers by the cart transportation agencies is generally as follows: each customer only needs to provide one sheng of rice, and the agency provides side dishes and accommodation free of charge. The cart transportation agencies "number" them according to their arrival order, and then assign business according to the order of each person's number. Most of the rice is brought from their homes, so even if they cannot find work immediately, they do not have much to spend and can wait quietly.

What benefits do the cart transportation agencies get from providing this convenience to them? The benefits are considerable. The farmers are generally required to give 20% of their income to the cart transportation agency as a commission. If a farmer earns two dollars, forty cents of silver must be taken from his own pocket and given to the cart transportation agency owner. Although the owner provides some side dishes, these dishes are so rough that they are only worth a few copper coins, and it would not matter if they were not recorded in the accounts. In short, the owner gets a considerable benefit.

The wages for pushing a "pierhead cart" are generally calculated based on the weight carried and the distance traveled. Generally, carrying a weight of about two hundred jin to a place about one hundred li away cannot be less than one dollar and fifty cents to two dollars. If wealthy people want to take a cart home for the New Year, they will ask for a few more cents, or at least ask for a few cents for wine money (these carts can be padded with quilts to make seats, which can be leaned on, and are very comfortable to walk on on flat ground). As for tea money, food money, and lodging money along the way, although there are also clear stipulations that they are "all-inclusive" and will not be

Continued on page 5

Page 23

Page 24

Page 25

taken care of, in the end, they are allowed to freeload on them because they are small amounts.

Pushing this kind of "pierhead cart" is mostly very hard work. Although they are old hands at pushing carts and know the "trick," pushing several hundred jin of weight for more than a hundred li a day is not an easy task. Most of these farmers who are good at pushing carts live in the mountains. They are used to walking in the mountains and have been learning to push carts since they were young. Moreover, whether it is a big or small task, they almost always use carts. For them, carrying with a "carrying pole" is not as convenient as pushing with a cart. Except for harvesting rice, when "bundles of rice stalks" must be carried, they usually push rice with a cart, push bricks and tiles with a cart, push cotton with a cart... Not to mention that, they even push manure with a cart. Under such extremely skilled conditions, the hardship of pushing "pierhead carts" should be greatly reduced, but every time I see their panting and the bean-sized beads of sweat on their foreheads, I cannot help but feel a sense of sympathy. Moreover, their income is really meager. They first have to spend a lot of rice waiting for business. After finally waiting for their number to be called, they push for more than two hundred li, which is only about four dollars. The cart transportation agency takes away eighty cents, leaving little for themselves. Moreover, although they only push for more than two hundred li, they have actually walked more than four hundred li, because this is a round trip, not a one-way trip!

Not only that, in Anqing, if there are few people, there is also the danger of being bullied by vagrants. They are already very poor, but there are still those who bully them and try to extort money from them. But in matters concerning them, there are always many people, and they all have a "cart pole" and some "brute force," so they are not easily defeated. In the past, there have been incidents of vagrants provoking them, but in the end, they defeated the invaders and obtained peace.

Interviews with Famous People

Interview with Zhou Leshan 205

—

I met Mr. Zhou Leshan at a banquet hosted by my old classmate Mr. Zhu.

One cold winter evening, in a certain room of Tongxing Building, there were many people, mostly young people. At that time, there was a gentleman who was a little older, with a rectangular face, wearing a leather coat, and looking a bit like a professor, who was talking about the love problems of young people in a corner of the room. Several listeners were nodding and smiling, as if his words were touching the hearts of young people. Through Mr. Zhu's introduction, I learned that this was the writer Mr. Zhou Leshan. At that time, I remembered the scene he described in "A Woman's Confession" of playing in a massage parlor, and I couldn't help but laugh.

After the initial introduction, the impression he gave me was indeed very deep. I only felt that he was a writer who met the ideals of young people, and his stuttering was something I would never forget.

Last week, the No. 10 public bus took me to Jiaozhou Road. With a hopeful heart, I walked into Yuan Yang Village.

"Ding...ding..." I pressed the doorbell.

"Who is it?" A child's voice.

"It's me."

A face of eleven or twelve years old looked out from the gap in the iron gate.

"Is Mr. Zhou at home?"

"Yes."

Opening the stern iron gate, I walked into a small bourgeois-style living room.

"Dad, someone has come to see you," the little brother shouted at the foot of the escalator.

Two small bourgeois met. After we greeted each other, he offered me a cigarette, and the maid poured tea.

"Is Mr. Zhou writing?" I asked.

"No, where did so many materials come from? I was just reading a book on 'Vitalism'."

"Oh, the author of this book is really a clever person. He came to our school last year to give a lecture. I remember the topic was 'A Scientific Analysis of Propriety, Justice, Integrity, and Shame.' At that time, none of the more than two thousand students in the entire auditorium were not listening with great interest."

"He is indeed knowledgeable, but judging from his book on 'Vitalism,' it seems that he speaks a bit too complex."

"Mr. Zhou, I heard that you are going abroad to study. Is that true?" I changed the topic.

"Yes, I plan to go to Japan. If the circumstances permit, I would also like to take a trip to Nanyang."

Speaking of Nanyang, it reminded me of his recent past article "Scenery of the Southern Country" published in the "Qingguang" column of the Shishi Xinbao.

"Mr. Zhou, what was your intention in writing that article 'Scenery of the Southern Country'?"

"Speaking of the intention of writing that humble work, I'm afraid you will laugh. The reason is that I have a great interest in the mysterious Nanyang and often fantasize about it. In order to wish me success in going to Nanyang, I boldly wrote this thing."

"This is not nonsense. When your masterpiece was published in 'Qingguang,' no matter how busy I was, I had to read it every day, otherwise I would feel like something was not finished, because I was also dreaming of traveling to Nanyang."

"You are flattering me too much, making me feel ashamed."

The needle of the self-ringing clock ran around once.

"I have taken up a lot of your time, I am very sorry."

"You're welcome."

Full of joy, I resigned and came out, sitting in the car, still savoring the excitement he gave me.
