Biographies of Famous People

Biography of Einstein (4) 207

— From Wood

In Einstein's three main papers of 1905—the one on the quantum theory of the photoelectric effect, the one on the molecular theory of Brownian motion, and the one on the special theory of relativity in electrodynamics—the one on quantum theory went beyond Planck's concept of energy quanta, which was introduced in 1900 in the theory of thermal radiation, and only treated as a special hypothesis in the phenomenon of thermal radiation. It expanded the generally recognized range to light emission phenomena and photoelectric phenomena. In 1907, it unexpectedly developed in the theory of specific heat, explaining that the specific heat of solids at low temperatures does not follow the Dulong–Petit law. His thoroughgoing discontinuity theory gave a sense of innovation to physics at that time.

There is no need to comment here that the paper on Brownian motion had already resonated with Smoluchowski's 1906 paper.

In Einstein's 1905 paper on the electrodynamics of moving bodies, the famous space-time transformation formula was published by Lorentz as early as May 1904 in the journal of the Amsterdam Academy of Sciences, in a paper with the same title. Originally, Einstein lived in a remote place and had not heard of Lorentz's paper, so his discovery can of course be said to be an independent discovery. However, the priority of this discovery is with Lorentz, so later this transformation formula was called the Lorentz transformation formula. However, Lorentz arbitrarily and expediently introduced this transformation formula in the electrodynamics of moving bodies. Einstein, on the other hand, saw it from a fundamental examination of the so-called "relativity of simultaneity," and therefore his paper contained important principles in addition to the results of the so-called transformation formula.

If we want to briefly describe the situation in the academic community regarding this issue before and after the publication of Einstein's paper, then this period should be called the era of "reinforcement work" on Lorentz's electron theory. Lorentz's electron theory appeared after Maxwell's electromagnetic theory. Regarding the discovery of the properties of electron-like electrical atoms, there was also its prehistory in electrical decomposition, cathode rays, electrical conduction theory, and optical dispersion theory. Lorentz's electron theory of this theory was disseminated in 1895, and it immediately received brilliant support in 1897 due to the discovery of the Zeeman effect. Secondly, the discovery of the need gave significant evidence in showing the reality of electrons. Therefore, the view that matter is only composed of positive and negative electricity gradually became powerful.

Lorentz's electron theory was based on the so-called absolutely forbidden ether, and solved various difficult problems in the electrodynamics of moving systems. However, if the ether is absolutely stationary and does not move with the movement of objects, then the principle of action and reaction, which is one of the fundamental principles of Newtonian mechanics, cannot be established between the object and the ether. It also contradicts the Michelson-Morley experiment (discovering the relative motion of the ether and the Earth) and does not conform to the mechanical principle of relativity. If we want to explain this issue in a little more detail, then the mechanical principle of relativity is based on the mechanics of Galileo and Newton, and the overall movement of an object system cannot be measured in internal mechanical experiments. However, if we imagine the so-called absolutely forbidden ether as Lorentz did, then that kind of movement can be measured optically. In this sense, Michelson and Morley carried out their experiment, but the result was negative, that is, we must admit that the same mechanical principle of relativity can be established optically. Therefore, in the 1895 paper, Lorentz also put forward the famous Lorentz contraction hypothesis, saying that everything moving in space, that is, in the ether, must be sensitive to this contraction, so that its uniform motion cannot be detected optically, thus avoiding the conflict with the Michelson-Morley experiment. He believed that everything from the smallness of electrons to the greatness of the Earth is subject to this contraction.

Einstein's 1905 paper said that the principle of relativity is also established in electrodynamics, taking the transformation of time and space in stationary and moving systems as the basis and postulate, and deductively deduced the Lorentz contraction theory.

Lorentz did not thoroughly investigate the relativity of time (simultaneity) as Einstein did, but Lorentz and Einstein gave the same results for the relationship between the mass and velocity of electrons.

However, in 1902 and 1903, Abraham, in his paper "The Mechanics of Electrons," believed that electrons are naturally constituted units, are rigid bodies that cannot be contracted, and opposed the Lorentz contraction theory. Consequently, he also questioned the correctness of the Michelson-Morley experiment. In the end, he did not follow the mechanical principle of relativity, but based on Lorentz's initial absolutism, and under the investigation that the emotions of matter are only entirely of electromagnetic origin, the result of the calculation showed the so-called longitudinal mass and transverse mass of the electron, and calculated the relationship with these velocities.

Professor Planck of Berlin considered Einstein's paper to be of great significance and wrote him a letter to express his admiration. Also, at the Berlin Physical Society in March 1906, Planck published a famous paper based on Einstein's paper, which recorded his equations of motion.

At the conference of physical scientists and medical scientists held in Stuttgart in September 1906, Planck, based on the above-mentioned equations of motion, published a paper calculating the results of Kaufmann's experiment. The result of the recalculation still leaned towards Abraham's theory. However, Planck was not satisfied with this. He wanted to obtain theoretical superiority in the method of Lorentz and Einstein and hoped for further experiments.

After this, a debate ensued between Planck, Kaufmann, Abraham, and others. Kaufmann said that Einstein's theory of relativity is only a theory of relativity for uniformly moving bodies, not an epistemologically thorough theory of relativity. Jun Machfield jokingly said that people over the age of forty maintain the mechanical theory of relativity, while people under the age of forty support the electrical theory of absolutism, and that he himself belongs to the latter. This made the entire audience laugh...

At the German Science and Medicine Conference in Dresden in September 1907, only Jun Machfield raised a question in a small report about Einstein's paper denying signals exceeding the speed of light. Other than that, there was no discussion about the theory of relativity and absolutism. However, in this year, Einstein published a comprehensive report on the theory of relativity in the German "Annual Report of Radiology and Electronics," and in its final chapter, he proposed a part of the discussion on expanding the theory of relativity to uniformly accelerated motion.

By the time of the German Science and Medicine Conference in September 1908, the situation was the exact opposite of the previous two years, and the theory of relativity had achieved absolute victory.

Why did 𡝰娜 Come Back? 208

— First

"Where did 𡝰娜 go?"—When the second sister came back, these seven words were written on the desk, lying sloppily on half a crumpled piece of paper, looking very dejected, and with such a question mark: like a round, wide-open eye, with a large tear just about to fall from the eye.

The second sisters pretended not to notice, still playfully joking. But Lan couldn't help but scold. The second sister also frowned and said: Why blame her for no reason; she cannot tolerate anyone adding insult to injury.

In fact, the second sister certainly forgave Lan in her heart. She was certainly right, she loved her eldest sister. Indeed, how gentle and amiable the eldest sister was! Who wouldn't want a lovely person to enjoy happiness in this world? Lan only knew to worry about her! The suffering that would immediately befall her.

The second sister loved the eldest sister even more. Only the second sister, who had endured all the torments of the world, could understand the pain deep in the eldest sister's heart, could deeply sympathize with it. Lan thought: The eldest sister's husband loves her, she should leave home—a home with a son, a daughter, and loving bliss. But Lan didn't know: The eldest sister only received her husband's love, the family's love, because she was docilely obedient. If she were not docilely obedient to him, he would not love her either. She thought: Is a woman's meaning in life only to be loved by her husband? Even teaching children, handling household affairs, and his unfaithfulness in love—having relationships with other women—must all be listened to one by one, bending to the will of the husband; isn't a woman just a machine? She didn't want to be a machine. She said to the second sister; she wanted to properly be a "person," living a "human life."

But Lan would not know that the eldest sister had so many unspeakable grievances. She only thought that after leaving the family; she would shed tears because she missed her children; she would feel lonely and sad; and she would live a long dissolute life, how painful a wandering life is—like the second sister, how lonely! How pitiful!

In fact, the eldest sister never felt that the third sister was lonely or in pain. On the contrary, she greatly envied the second sister's freedom! Therefore, time finally gave her this courage; she resolutely wanted to escape that prison-like family.

She only told the second sister her decision to leave. After the second sister raised many objections and issues of pros and cons, and discussed them with her, she knew that her determination this time was not an impulsive decision. She agreed with her "properly being a 'person' and living a 'human' life." So she no longer used negative language to dissuade her, losing her courage.

They quietly prepared, without telling Lan; on the 4:15 pm express train, she sent her eldest sister out of Shanghai.

When she came back, Lan scolded her for doing such a rash thing. The eldest sister's husband even more fiercely hated her, asking her for his wife. She only pretended that it was none of her business, that she didn't know anything, and they couldn't find her. What she was planning in her heart was only how to find work for her eldest sister; how to write letters to comfort her and encourage her. —What can be done? Women have to struggle, to properly be "people," to live independently, suffering, they must endure love. Whether spiritually or physically, they must endure immeasurable pain. But the eldest sister and the second sister said: This kind of suffering is suffering for freedom, meaningful, and valuable. The second sister could only use these empty words to encourage her, to comfort her.

Empty talk is ultimately empty talk, would the second sister forget the lessons that reality had taught her? But, she couldn't bear to stop a person in hell, eagerly yearning for the light of a new ideal life; and she couldn't find a reason to stop her from returning to what the eldest sister considered an unbearable place——improper love, and an incompatible life.

"This is bound to happen, let it go with time"—This was the second sister's attitude. But she also knew: There were only a few people who sympathized with the eldest sister and helped her. Society, the masses, who could care about her pain? Unless she bore all the suffering herself, there was no help at all. Then, the eldest sister, as fragile as she was, could not be as strong as the second sister, able to clash head-on with gales and storms!

Therefore, inevitably, the eldest sister finally came back—was brought back by her husband. The secret address was written by the second sister, it could also be said that it was "deceived" out of her by the husband. But the second sister had already understood; whether she was suspected, cursed, or despised, she didn't care. Her heart was as calm as ever. —She had no joyful excitement, nor bitter depression.

It's just that, the second sister no longer often went to the eldest sister's home. She knew that the eldest sister's heart was even more painful, she couldn't bear to touch a woman's heart that didn't want to be numb but couldn't help but be numb!

"Where did 𡝰娜 go!" But 𡝰娜 came back again! Why did 𡝰娜 want to come back? Gales and storms bullied her; open spears and hidden arrows wounded her; the dead end of life threatened her; the etiquette and religious environment oppressed her. The fragile her, injured and damaged, did not possess all the weapons to resist the strong enemy, she inevitably came back!

Shen Bao Local Supplement Movie Special

Male and Female Actors Whose Luck Began After Fifty (Middle) 214

— Ti Yun

May Robson also said: "I have been an actor for fifty years, and I now feel as strong as I was fifty years ago, when I first appeared on stage in London. Of course, my view of life is not as serious as it used to be. The maturity of age has pointed out a path of optimism and acceptance, and has cultivated a sense of humor. A person's brain should not decline due to old age. I have seen so many changes in my life. The stage always reflects the myriad things of the world, and the myriad things of the world are always spinning. And I have been able to see the changes in the myriad things of the world on the stage, and I feel that is my luck. But there must be many changes that will continue to unfold before our eyes today and in the future, and I am certainly willing to live and watch. When the war continues, a person will never put down his weapons and run away, unless he is a coward. I will never be a coward. I quietly await the summons of death."

Fifty years ago, Mary Robison first appeared on stage in a small theater in London. At that time, the person writing the program was careless and missed a letter in each word of her name, writing her fragrant name as (May Robson). May Robson simply made a mistake and used that name, all the way to the present. Her arrival in Hollywood was recommended by the late Queen Mother Mary Tramp. After Mary Tramp's death, May Robson became the only old female role in Hollywood. She has already gained fame in "Lady for a Day." Now her new film (Lay by Choice) is also a strong work.

There is a Henrietta Crossman. She first appeared on stage as far back as 1883. After many hardships, she gradually became a famous actress. Climbing the ladder of fame is slow and difficult, but she actually climbed to the highest level. At that time, her hair had already turned from golden yellow to gray, but the audience in New York saw her take the stage and everyone stood up and cheered. She became famous. She was it. When she retired, she had stood on the stage for half a century. She then bought a large house and settled down with her husband. Unexpectedly, the turmoil in the exchange market arose, and the land under Henrietta's feet was completely swept away. Although she had a large house to live in, she had no money to live on. Later, forced by hunger and cold, she had to put on makeup and return to the stage, becoming a widow again. Fox Company, admiring her fame, hired her. She occupies a very important position in (Menacz), but it has been sixty-five years since she first came into the world!

Alison Skipworth is now fifty-five years old, but she has only become popular in recent years. She enjoyed twenty-five years of fame on Broadway in New York. She has a bright singing voice, and has also tried to appear on the screen, but in the silent film era, although she had a natural singing voice, she had no place to use her talents. After the invention of sound films, she jumped to become a singing old female role. She occupies a very important position in singer Bing Crosby's (Here is my heart). The following are some recent talks by Alison.

"Many people ask me, since you already have a lot of money and can live a happy life, why don't you retire? But if I retire and don't do anything, how can I spend my days? Who is willing to sit at home by themselves, just thinking that she is an old woman? Many people worry about age, and their age has not reached old age, but they are already old. That's because they sit in a rocking chair all day long, thinking, thinking, thinking. I remember a friend who, when the New York subway was just being laid, said to himself: "They want to build a subway. I don't know if I will be able to see it built." Now that the subway has been built, it has been several decades, and my friend is still alive and has not died. If he was not afraid of death and came out to do something, then he would have accomplished a lot in these decades.

I like to work. Work can make a person's body strong, and it can also make a person's brain flexible. Age is not calculated by time. Age is related to thought. A person who is sixty years old may be very young, but a person who is twenty years old may already be old. I worry about those people who are always worried about dying of old age. As far as I am concerned, I don't have time to fantasize. My work, my games, have kept me busy enough. I also don't reminisce about the past and grieve. I only know how to think about the future. I want to stand in this place until no one wants me anymore (To be continued)

Movie Reviews

Review of "A Lost Lady" 215

— Ling He

A Lost Lady - Cathay

It is almost unnecessary to explain that the playwright's outdated view of love under the definition of love and duty, which is beneficial to the existing social system, will not be ignored by anyone who has seen this film. After watching, the story here is like this:

Mary's fiancé died, and she felt completely hopeless, vowing never to speak of love again. Soon, a middle-aged famous lawyer fell in love with her. Although she was confident that there was no love between her and him, she still married him to repay his kindness. Of course, the most important thing was because the lawyer was rich. After the marriage, she and her husband enjoyed themselves to the fullest. The husband made her a new house, and there was also a garden. The couple, whose ages were very different, seemed to be living very peacefully. But she also accidentally met a pilot, and there was a love entanglement, which changed her life, like a calm water surface broken by a stone. On the one hand, she had the responsibility of a wife to her husband, and on the other hand, she was entangled in love. Under this contradictory mood, she felt great pain, which made her drink madly, abuse her body, and finally ask her husband for a divorce. Naturally, this made the lawyer feel the greatest embarrassment. In a very painful mood, he fainted from excessive stimulation. So Mary realized that her responsibility was even greater, and she had to serve her husband day and night, until her husband was critically ill, when she began to sincerely love her husband. (The brochure does not say so)

In such a story, in addition to illustrating the playwright's old-fashioned views, the main thing is to make women submit to their husbands, sacrifice their own love, and sacrifice their own happiness. After Ibsen's Nora walked out of the doll's house and discussed where Nora was going, we unexpectedly saw this film that advises women to return to their families! In the past, some people vigorously advocated the supremacy of love, which was not necessarily progressive at a certain stage, but now it has been hit by the times, but "A Lost Lady" can't even catch up with the supremacy of love.

However, this film, due to the excellent skills of the playwright and director, has deeply imprinted the film's internal content into the hearts of every audience. Very clearly, the playwright deeply depicted Marlene's inner world, giving the audience a deep impression of her. What is even more worthy of praise is the technique of the director Alfred E Green, who not only made the story very simple based on the compactness of the script, but also played the part of the play very competently and happily. The most brilliant thing is Marlene's painful drinking, and the lawyer's sleepless night, leaving early in the morning, all the way to not being able to support himself in court and fainting. These places are very successful. At the same time, we will not ignore the excellent acting skills of Barbara Stanwyck and Frank Morgan, (but Ricardo Cortez did not succeed due to not being suitable for the personality, he could not pretend to be a suave young man at all, although he had very good results in the past, such as City Symphony.) This kind of achievement cannot be done by mediocre actors. However, we recognize that "success" and "good" seem to be different. In other words, the film's expression technique is successful, but based on a certain point of view and our subjective judgment, we cannot say that this is a "good" film.

A Review of "Springtime in My Heart" 216

— You Jing

Here is My Heart

Radiance of Great Light

Following "She Knew All the Answers," Bing Crosby and Kitty Carlisle are back with "Springtime in My Heart." It's also touted as a showcase for singing.

Here, naturally, given the class nature of their songs and to cater to their audience's tastes, they inevitably fabricate a hollow and luxurious story to contain it. At the same time, there's a real sense that the reality of the luxurious lifestyle that could be sung about, the glory that could be extolled, has become a fleeting dream. Therefore, what's fabricated here also has to be impoverished princesses and fallen nobles, these poor aristocrats, to harmonize with the passionate and melancholic melodies they sing, seeking a good fit and satisfying the mood of the wealthy in their twilight years. It's further self-deprecating in its portrayal of a famous singer who condescends to work as a servant, actually wins the love of a princess, is then abandoned, and finally has to return to her embrace in a jesting performance.

Starting from this premise, the entire performance is supported by an atmosphere of childish pranks and nonsense throughout. From Hao Sen fishing a small fish out of the Atlantic Ocean, the erotic pursuit in front of the elevator, the drunken state of the real servant, the ugly behavior of the fake servant, the perverted sexuality of the maid, the embarrassment of the fallen nobles, to the movements of cats, dogs, and birds, everything is made comical to elicit laughter from the audience with so-called gags. Thus, the producer's goal is achieved amidst the audience's laughter.

Naturally, we shouldn't forget the songs, which are the main part of this film. There are three songs: "It's June in January," "With Every Breath I Take," and "Love is Just Around the Corner." Just like the success of the "gags" in the dialogue and action, the songs are also sung successfully. As for the meaning of so-called success, when understood in the context of the entire film, we cannot give it a higher evaluation.

Director Frank Tuttle forcefully completed this empty story, making it into the shape it should be.

Both lead actors performed well. Kitty Carlisle, in particular, had more inner expression.

Gong Jianong Sacrifices Himself for His Son 217

In Li Pingqian's film "Human Relations," Gong Jianong plays a construction worker who likes to drink and gamble, which leads to his wife leaving him, his family falling apart, and him going to jail. When he is released after twenty years, he works as a servant in the bank his son owns. However, due to the circumstances, he cannot tell his son that he is his father.

One day, he learns that his son is going to transport a batch of funds to another location, and he also knows that his son will first go to a hotel before departing. He further knows that once he arrives at the hotel, he will inevitably be ambushed by villains. He rushes to the hotel, and indeed, his son's funds are robbed. Therefore, he disregards everything and snatches the funds back and flees. As he escapes out the door, he is shot dead by the police. But no one knows that he sacrificed himself for his son, rather than being a thief. (Question)

Movie Novel

National Cry (Bordertown) (II) 218

— Xuemei

Johnny Ramirez spoke to the judge: "Your Honor, the simple facts of this case have been stated, and therefore I feel that I have an important duty to my client and to the court, which must be stated again. I have discovered that the defendant's car is not insured, but she has repeatedly caused accidents, one after another...". The defendant's lawyer listened and immediately stood up to speak: "I object to this statement. I ask the court to forbid it." The judge, like an echo, immediately declared: "Objection sustained."

Johnny knew he had no other choice but to obey the judge's will. He then continued patiently: "Your Honor, according to the court's will, but there is a second point. At the time of this accident, nine-tenths of the defendant was under the influence of alcohol. In other words, the defendant was indeed excessively drunk and caused the disaster..." The defendant's lawyer heard this and stood up again to speak: "I object to that." But he said it with a smile. "Opposing counsel's statement is completely unfounded and has nothing to do with this case; furthermore, there is now no witness who can testify to the defendant's condition at the time." The judge then declared again: "Objection sustained."

Johnny Ramirez was a little anxious now. He said: "But, Your Honor, I just want to prove..." The judge interrupted him before he could finish speaking, saying: "This court is aware of what counsel intends, but counsel should understand that this court is not some kind of law school. Before coming to court, you should have had adequate preparation for the case..." The judge was relaxed, without a bead of sweat on his brow; the defendant's lawyer was the same. He was well prepared, his hair neatly combed, his beard cleanly shaved. Although they may not necessarily be looking at each other and smiling, they were kindred spirits, looking down on this disheveled, poor lawyer from Sonora, not giving him a chance to speak.

Finally, Johnny could no longer endure it. His strong ethnicity burst forth involuntarily. He said loudly: "Does the court not want to know the truth? Does the court not want to uphold justice? Does the court not know that this poor old man's car was wrecked by a drunken woman, so that his livelihood was destroyed by a spoiled woman? She thinks she has money and doesn't care if she kills someone. But in this court, what is more important? A few specialized legal terms, or the real situation?"

Johnny's words caused everyone in the courtroom to look at each other in dismay, but if Johnny thought he could reason his way through this place, he was wrong. Because the judge had already made a solemn statement. He said: "This court is of course very concerned about the truth, but from the mouth of someone who speaks recklessly, speaks vulgarly, and shows his feelings... um... a lawyer, this court cannot accept it. Therefore, this court must point out that since counsel did not have adequate preparation beforehand, you have committed professional negligence towards your client. This case is dismissed for lack of evidence!"

Everything was over. The judge had already retreated into the chambers. The old farmer stood beside Johnny, anxiously asking: "Johnny, is my car fixed? Did you win the case for me?" At this moment, the black-haired woman quietly walked behind Johnny and touched his arm. Johnny turned his head, frowning as he looked at her. The woman, whose name was Diane Ahern, said: "Perhaps you won't believe it, but I'm willing to help your client and get his car fixed. I understand, even though the judge... Do you think that's alright?..." As she spoke, she smiled sweetly, took out a large roll of banknotes, and reached out to give them to Johnny. Who could resist her smile? He began to smile. He thanked her, saying: "You're so kind..." Before he could finish speaking, her lawyer, Brooke, had already come up and stopped her, saying: "Diane, are you crazy? Giving him money is the same as admitting your responsibility. Aren't you afraid he'll sue you in criminal court?" (To be continued)
